Aftermath in Northern Fujian Divided into Five Zones

Refugees Flock Back to Their Native Places

Fuzhou Correspondence: After the successive recovery of Chong'an, Guangze, Shaowu, Jiangle, Jianning, and Taining counties in northern Fujian, refugees who had fled to Nanping and Jian'ou counties have been allocated 6,000 yuan by the Red Disaster Relief Association. Kang Shaozhou, a member of the Provincial Party Department, and Lin Jinan, a member of the Provincial Government, have been dispatched to handle the repatriation to help them make a living. There are also about a thousand refugees who fled to Fuzhou. Now that the early rice is ripening, they are eager to return to their hometowns to harvest it. However, the steamboats operating upstream are taking advantage of this opportunity to raise prices, exceeding the original fare by more than double. Refugee groups from various counties have sent representatives to request relief from the Relief Association. The association has negotiated with the upstream steamboat association to reduce the fare by half, with the association issuing certificates for boarding. However, the steamboats are limited in capacity and cannot accommodate everyone, so repatriation began on the 6th in batches of one hundred people each. The association is also providing hard biscuits as rations and sending personnel to care for them on their journey. It is expected that the repatriation will be completed by the end of this month. However, the people of Ninghua, Changting, Liancheng, and Guihua counties in western Fujian are once again fleeing to Yong'an and Shaxian counties due to the intrusion of Red bandits from the Jiangxi border, and have telegraphed the province for relief. The Relief Association is currently coordinating measures. On the military front, the newly formed Second Division, under Lu Xingbang, is responsible for blocking the bandits. According to a telegram from Division Commander Lu to the province yesterday, the Sixth Brigade of his division, under Lu Xinming, has advanced towards Liancheng, the Fifth Brigade, under Ye Xingjin, towards Qingliu, and the Fourth Brigade, under Lu Xingrong, towards Guihua. He has requested that Zhang Zhen, commander of the 49th Division, also send troops to Shanghang and Wuping to jointly intercept the bandits. As for the aftermath in northern Fujian and the suppression of remaining bandits, these matters are being handled by Liu Heding, commander of the 56th Division. The area has been divided into five zones: the first zone, Jian'ou and Pucheng, is under the responsibility of Lin Bingzhou's brigade; the second zone, Shaowu and Chong'an, is under the responsibility of Qian Yuguang's brigade; the third zone, Jianning and Taining, is under the responsibility of Zhou Zhiqun's brigade; the fourth zone, Jiangle and Shunchang, is under the responsibility of Gui Zhenyuan's brigade; and the fifth zone, Yanping, is under the responsibility of Liu Shangzhi's brigade. In addition, Jiang Yan's brigade is serving as a reserve force to support the various zones. Liu Heding himself traveled from Yanping to the Shunchang area on the 5th to inspect the defense, and the local situation is still considered peaceful. (August 7th)

Cantonese Bandits Repeatedly Bomb Ferries

Two Ferries, one in Zhaoqing and one in Dongguan, were successively bombed by bandits

Eight Killed and Injured on the Dongguan Ferry, Six Injured on the Zhaoqing Ferry

Guangzhou Correspondence: Due to recent military tensions in Guangdong, the frequent movement of local defense forces has led to increased activity by local bandits. Furthermore, river and sea pirates have become rampant again. In recent days, there have been reports of ferries being bombed, causing travelers to lament the dangerous conditions. On the evening of the 3rd of this month, the "Tong'an Ferry," traveling between Guangzhou and Zhaoqing, arrived in Guangzhou from Zhaoqing. While docked at the Chao Yin Street Pier on the Bund and passengers were disembarking, bandits suddenly seized the opportunity amidst the noise and secretly placed a bomb under the grand staircase of the Tong'an Ferry's cabin. At 11:40 PM, while passengers had not yet completely disembarked, the bomb exploded with a loud bang, creating a hole approximately two feet square in the cabin floor and destroying several steps. After investigation, a fragment of the bomb and a business card from the "Haiqiang Hall" bandit gang were found at the scene. The ship owner reported the incident to the Haizhu Branch Bureau. During the explosion, Chen Jiu, a ship's assistant, was seriously injured on the right arm, which was nearly broken, and his life is in danger. Another man, Liang Er, suffered injuries all over his body. In addition, Xia Wenshi, a female passenger, suffered leg injuries; Zhang Chenshi suffered injuries to her lower back; a coolie named Huang Fang suffered injuries to his right leg; and a passenger named Li Miaobi suffered injuries to his lower back and legs. In total, six people were injured. The morning after this incident (the morning of the 4th), the "Taisheng" ferry, traveling between Dongguan and Guangzhou, was also bombed by bandits en route. When the ship departed from Guangzhou at 6:15 AM on the 4th, nothing seemed amiss. However, when it reached the river surface near the Chebei Estuary Pagoda on Pazhou Island (under the jurisdiction of Panyu), a loud explosion suddenly occurred in the passenger cabin, killing two passengers instantly. Their flesh was mangled beyond recognition, a truly horrific sight. Six people were also injured at the same time. The deceased included a man resembling a soldier, about twenty years old, whose name was unknown. He was wearing a cloth undershirt and white cloth trousers. His head and both hands were blown off, and his chest and heart were injured. The wounds were charred and bloody. The other deceased, also an unknown male passenger about twenty years old, had his left forehead blown open, and his left flank had a wound about three inches wide, with intestines protruding. His skin was broken and charred. As the names and addresses of the above two individuals are unknown, and no relatives have claimed their bodies, the ship owner has temporarily provided coffins and buried them. In addition, six people were injured, and the investigation revealed the following: (1) Luo Bing, 36 years old, from Gaozhou, suffered injuries to his left and right legs and front arms; (2) Ren Shimei, 16 years old, from Dongguan, suffered facial injuries; (3) Huang Aying suffered injuries to his abdomen and elbows; (4) Zhang Ye, 51 years old, from Dongguan, suffered injuries to his head and left upper arm; (5) Ding Fa, 55 years old, from Dongguan, suffered injuries to his head, face, and left forehead; (6) Guo Ke, 30 years old, from Hunan, suffered injuries to his left upper arm. (August 4th)

Sino-French Academic Expedition

The Resolution of the Dispute

A Letter from Chu Minyi in Jiuquan to an Important Figure

Bu An Dismissed, Pei Wenming Apologized, and the Matter Was Resolved

Both Parties Re-Sign a New Cooperation Agreement

Continuing the Expedition, Heading Directly to Hami via the Desert

The Sino-French Academic Expedition encountered a dispute among its members, with the Chinese member Hao Jingsheng being beaten by the French team leader Bu An. This incident raised concerns about national dignity, and fueled by patriotic sentiments, coupled with the presence of a Yellow Race Inspection Team in Paris, there was growing dissatisfaction domestically. Although the Chinese team leader Chu Minyi sent numerous telegrams, initially advocating withdrawal and then reporting that the dispute had been resolved, the details of the dispute and the resolution remained unknown to the outside world. Yesterday, a certain important figure received a letter from Chu, providing a detailed account of the incident: "I sent a letter from Bailing Temple, and a month has passed since then. Although the journey was extremely arduous, I arrived safely in Jiuquan on June 15th. After arriving, I negotiated with the French side and sent telegrams to the central government and the French ambassador through the Ancient Relics Preservation Committee. I believe these have been reported in the newspapers. Today, the negotiations with the French side have been satisfactory, so I have again telegraphed the central government and the French ambassador, reporting that the dispute between the two parties has been resolved satisfactorily. We are scheduled to proceed westward at 6:00 AM tomorrow, but we have decided not to go through Anxi but to continue through the desert to Hami. The recent cause of the Sino-French dispute lies with Mr. Hao Jingsheng. He was beaten and humiliated by Mr. Bu An at Hoyomoto on a certain day. The reasons for the beating are twofold: First, Chinese and Western customs differ, and once they embark on a long journey together, disagreements and arguments are likely to arise. According to Teilhard de Chardin (a geologist and Catholic priest traveling with us), French people also had conflicts among themselves during their last trip to Africa. Moreover, when Chinese and French people travel together, there are differences in language (Mr. Hao does not understand French), temperament, and other factors, which can easily lead to disputes. Second, the hardships of desert life can also easily provoke nervous excitement. With a slight lack of patience, anger can erupt uncontrollably. Therefore, when Mr. Hao and Mr. Bu An were arguing before the beating, I tried to dissuade them, but Mr. Hao scolded me as a 'slave of a fallen nation.' I did not respond but avoided his anger. Therefore, I had already left the scene when Mr. Bu An beat Mr. Hao. Mr. Hao's rudeness is undeniable, and I was also scolded. How could I bear to see him beaten by foreigners? Furthermore, at that time, Mr. Hao and Mr. Zhou Bao Han had withdrawn in the desert. Before receiving telegrams from Mr. Hao and Mr. Zhou from Baotou (sent on June 14th and received here on June 20th), I was deeply concerned about their safety. That is why I said what I did in the telegram to the French ambassador. Now that Mr. Hao and Mr. Zhou have arrived in Beiping early, perhaps they think that I ignored this matter. They do not know that after I arrived in Suzhou, I convened a six-person meeting, and the vote on whether to advance or retreat was evenly divided (Jiao, Liu, and Chu advocated retreat and return to the east, while Yao, Yang, and Zheng advocated advance and travel west). After continued discussion, Mr. Zheng also expressed his willingness to return east with me. Therefore, we decided to separate from the French side. On the one hand, we telegraphed the central government for instructions, and on the other hand, we asked Commander Ma, the local commander, to persuade the French to stay here temporarily and not to send wireless telegrams. The French were greatly embarrassed and claimed to be prisoners, but in reality, Commander Ma treated the French very kindly. We told them that we had telegraphed the central government for instructions and that we would stay temporarily until the central government sent a telegram. However, the French were eager to leave and could not obtain permission from Commander Ma Bufang. The French threatened Commander Ma, but we were willing to take full responsibility and sent a letter to Commander Ma, listing the French violations of Sino-French cooperation. The French advanced, but we did not. Commander Ma believed that if we did not proceed, he naturally would not allow the French to travel alone. Therefore, he conveyed this idea to the French, and the French realized the situation, apologized in person, and re-signed seven articles of continued cooperation. The main points are: (1) Bu An was removed and replaced by Burll (Pei Wenming apologized to Jiao Jihua, but this was not included in the articles); (2) Past disputes would not be mentioned on the road but would be reserved for negotiations in Beiping upon our return; (3) If one party was unable to enter Xinjiang, both parties would not enter; (4) The transmission and reception of wireless telegrams would be publicly announced, and wireless telegrams would not be used where there were telegraph offices, etc., a total of seven articles. The original text is copied separately. The French all agreed, and all six people signed the document. Therefore, we continued cooperation and are scheduled to proceed west tomorrow morning, bypassing Anxi and heading directly to Hami.

The reason for the third article stipulating joint advance and retreat is that Envoy Wei telegraphed, saying that Xinjiang welcomes the French but absolutely rejects our countrymen, and advised us to stay on the Xinjiang-Gansu border and wait for the French to return east and take us back. This intention is truly an insult to the nation and violates not only Sino-French academic cooperation. Moreover, I received several telegrams from Xinjiang refusing the French entry and even regarding the former Northwest and the current Sino-French collaboration as inviting wolves into the house. How can there be a situation of welcoming foreigners but rejecting our own countrymen? We did not believe in such unreasonable words. Rather than being abandoned by the French in Gansu, it is better to stay in Suzhou and wait for the central government to approve our cancellation of the cooperation agreement and return east. For the past two days, the atmosphere has been extremely tense, and there was almost another major dispute. Fortunately, Commander Ma Zixiang supported us, and we were able to reach a continued cooperation agreement, preventing the Sino-French academic expedition of 1919 from failing.

The origin of this dispute lies in Bu An's stubbornness and abuse of power in beating people for no reason, Pei Wenming's arrogance, and Envoy Wei's intention to abandon the Chinese members on the border, violating the cooperation agreement. Now that both parties have re-signed supplementary articles, I hope that there will be no more disputes in the future. The purpose of this western expedition is simply to study academics and develop the Northwest. From a broader perspective, the French side is only using this opportunity to promote the ability of their crawling cars to traverse the desert. One or two curious people joined, merely wanting to see the exotic customs of the East. As for imperialist aggression, etc., that cannot be discussed. The origin of this dispute is due to the imperfect organization of this cooperative group (in fact, it is extremely difficult to perfect this kind of organization), and emotional impulses and disputes are unavoidable and can be regarded as normal. However, when the dispute occurred between people of two countries, it involved the insult of the group, and due to the excessive concern of patriotic hearts, suspicion was cast upon the aggression of imperialism. In reality, all of these are caused by the word "misunderstanding." We have examined the matter carefully and believe that it has not caused any harm to the country or individuals, and it does not violate justice or conscience. Therefore, we have no choice but to compromise. As for the excessive concerns and misunderstandings of the people, they will gradually understand the facts and will have no use for their excessive concerns. Minyi respectfully submits this on the evening of June 20th.

Appendix: Sino-French Continued Cooperation Methods for the 1919 Academic Expedition. (1) Please have Burll act as the French team leader until the meeting in Hadier. (2) Wireless telegram messages shall be announced at any time. Wireless telephones shall not be used in places in China where there are telegraph offices. (3) If one party is unable to enter Xinjiang, both parties shall not enter the country. (4) The situation encountered on the road in the past shall be temporarily reserved for negotiation, and shall no longer be mentioned on the road. (5) Future progress matters shall be discussed between the Chinese team leader and the French Acting Team Leader. (6) If opinions arise among the members of the team in the future, the Chinese team leader and the French Acting Team Leader shall consult and resolve them together, and shall not take direct action. (7) If both parties agree to this method, it shall be signed jointly by the six people Chu, Yao, Jiao on the Chinese side and Pu, Bu, and De on the French side, and each party shall keep a copy. June 20, 20th year of the Republic of China. Signed jointly by Bu An, Jiao Jihua, Chu Minyi, Yao Xijiu, Burll, and Teilhard de Chardin in Jiuquan.

Zhejiang Money Industry Requests Reduction of Business Tax Rate

The Department of Finance replied with disapproval

Wang Zhengying, Director of the Department of Finance of Zhejiang Province, recently sent a letter to the chambers of commerce of various cities and counties, stating that according to reports from various chambers of commerce, the money industry has petitioned to reduce the business tax rate in Zhejiang Province to the rate stipulated in Shanghai, and that since banks and money shops both belong to the financial industry, and banks are not currently subject to business tax, the business tax on money shops should not be reduced, which is unfair. After investigation, the original business tax rate for the money industry in Zhejiang Province was 2 per mille based on the capital amount. Later, the Ministry of Finance revised it to 10 per mille, and all provinces have followed this regulation. This is a general case, and it is difficult to make any changes. The situation regarding the business tax rate differs between provinces and Shanghai, and they cannot be compared. This is not only true for the money industry. This has been clearly announced in the past. If the business tax rate for the money industry is changed to the Shanghai rate, other industries will also request to follow suit, which will inevitably lead to numerous disputes. In fact, it is impossible to comply. Although banks are not subject to business tax, the income tax law has been promulgated by the central government. The amount of tax they bear will definitely not be lighter than the business tax on the money industry. Therefore, the so-called unfair method is no longer an issue. Currently, the financial situation is difficult, and there is an urgent need for funds. Colleagues in the money industry are mostly deeply aware of righteousness and public service, and will surely consider the difficult situation of the government and enthusiastically contribute. If the resistance of one industry leads to other industries following suit, affecting the progress of taxation, this would not be in line with the principle of money industry colleagues loving and protecting the government. The chamber of commerce is hereby requested to inform the money industry to promptly pay taxes at the stipulated rate and not to wait and see. If other provinces have alternative reduction methods for the business tax rate of the money industry in the future, Zhejiang Province will then follow suit. And hope to inform them, to show public friendship. (12th)

Attended by Jiangsu Province

Re-election Meeting of Delegates to the Fourth National Congress

Ma Yinbing and Others Elected

The re-election meeting of delegates from Jiangsu Province to the Fourth National Congress of the Kuomintang of China was held yesterday (the 12th) at 9:00 AM in the public lecture hall of Boxian Park. After the meeting was announced open, Yang Xingqin, a member of the provincial party affairs reorganization committee, gave a report, stating that today is the re-election meeting of delegates from Jiangsu Province to the Fourth National Congress of the Kuomintang of China. According to the central government's regulations, the province of sixty-one counties, generates a total of one hundred and twenty-four preliminary elected representatives. After two reviews by the Provincial Reorganization Committee, all representatives are qualified. Today, one hundred and twenty-one representatives are present, and the meeting can be convened in accordance with the law. Now, please elect a chairman. Representatives nominated Xie Chengyu and Zhang Renjie, and the central supervisor Wu put it to a vote. The result was that Xie Chengyu, a representative from Zhenjiang County, was elected as the chairman of the congress by a majority vote. The meeting was then held in accordance with the procedure, and the chairman reported that the process of the province's handling of this re-election meeting for the Fourth National Congress delegates would be briefly reported. After receiving the central government's decree on the election of delegates to the Fourth National Congress, the Provincial Party Affairs Reorganization Committee decided to implement the preliminary election in accordance with the central government's regulations because the lower-level party departments in Jiangsu Province had been established one after another, and the Provincial Congress was scheduled to be held on the 15th of this month. Based on the time calculation, the formal Executive Committee could only be established in September. If the election of delegates from the province to the Fourth National Congress had to wait for the establishment of the Executive Committee, the time would be too short, and there would be many inconveniences. After the method was decided, on the one hand, it was reported to the central government for approval, and on the other hand, supervisors were sent to various counties to supervise the election. Later, the central government repeatedly sent telegrams to the meeting, stipulating the election method, and also sent Comrade Wu Jiayou to the meeting to supervise the election. All the processes were roughly like this. Then, the central supervisor gave instructions and read out the election regulations. Finally, the election was held. The chairman appointed Zhang Zhaobo and Chen Shouyan as supervisors, Zhu Jiming and Chen Zhenbang as ballot counters, He Jin and Yang Yushu as ballot readers, and Zhao Jianhua and Zhang Renjie as ballot recorders. After the appointments, the ballots were distributed, and the results were as follows: (1) Ten delegates were elected: Ma Yinbing, 105 votes; Xie Chengyu, 69 votes; Wu Baofeng, 98 votes; Yang Xingqin, 68 votes; Ye Xiufeng, 82 votes; Ge Jianshi, 67 votes; Zhang Yuanyang, 76 votes; Huang Yuren, 62 votes; Qi Xiyong, 74 votes; Gu Ziyang, 60 votes; (2) The five candidates with the next highest number of votes: Zhou Shaocheng, 53 votes; Cao Minghuan, 51 votes; Zhu Jianbai, 48 votes; Zhou Houjun, 52 votes; Yu Huaizhong, 51 votes. After the election, the delegates gathered in front of the bronze statue of Zhao Sheng and took a photo before dispersing.

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Cutting Vegetables Leads to Beating and Injury: Xie Bochang and Zhou Shengyan, employees of the Sanyou Motor Company, went to the wasteland next to the railway water pavilion at 5:00 PM the day before yesterday to cut wild amaranth stems. A woman speaking with a Hakka accent came out to stop them, verbally abusing them. Xie and Zhou argued that the land was barren and the vegetables were wild, so anyone could cut them. The woman became furious and returned to the railway station, summoning seven or eight workers led by a worker surnamed Xie. They suddenly surrounded Xie and Zhou and beat them repeatedly. Then they tied them up, hung them on a tree, and beat them with iron rods and coal shovels. Villagers gathered to watch, but no one dared to step forward to stop them because the woman was so fierce. They reported to the Songjiang stationmaster, who arrived and stopped the beating. Worker Xie knew that he had caused trouble and insisted on escorting Xie and Zhou to Shanghai for investigation. After much persuasion, they were sent to Songjiang Hospital for treatment because Xie and Zhou had suffered serious injuries and needed immediate medical attention. It is reported that the villagers believe that the woman is the concubine of a certain worker and has repeatedly caused trouble. They have submitted a public report to the stationmaster requesting a strict investigation. Xie Bochang and Zhou Shengyan, who were injured, have also reported to the Ningbo-Shaoxing Association in Songjiang for assistance.

Aircraft Crash Damages Rice Fields: At 9:00 AM today (the 12th), a white aircraft from the Naval Command was flying back to Shanghai from Hangzhou when it suddenly experienced mechanical failure and landed near the railway in Xinqiao, damaging several acres of rice paddies. The pilot also suffered facial abrasions. Villagers gathered to watch, and the farmers whose rice fields had been damaged demanded compensation, claiming that their livelihood for the year and their ability to pay rent depended on the rice. The pilot agreed to compensate them, but there was a large difference in the amount of compensation offered. The villagers went to Songjiang County Government to report the matter, requesting the government to order the aircraft to be responsible for the compensation. County Magistrate Shen promised to investigate and instructed the villagers to return home. It is unknown how this will be resolved. It is reported that the aircraft damage is minor. The pilot has already taken a car to Shanghai. Police officers from the 10th Detachment are protecting the aircraft.

Suzhou

Department of Finance Urges Payment of Construction Bonds: The Jiangsu Provincial Government issued construction bonds, and Wuxian County was allocated 200,000 yuan. Former County Magistrate Huang convened meetings of local figures, but there were no results. The gentry believed that the construction bonds were used for construction in Jiangbei and had nothing to do with Wuxian County, so they could not use the money from Wuxian County for construction in other counties. Therefore, they jointly telegraphed the provincial government requesting exemption, but this was not approved. Former Director Yuan of the Finance Bureau also resigned due to the difficulty in raising funds. Yesterday, the Finance Bureau received a telegram from the Department of Finance urging payment by August 30th. Director Shen of the new bureau telegraphed the Department of Finance, requesting that the Construction Bureau be jointly responsible for handling the matter.

Appeal Judgment in Murder Case of Squad Leader: Zhang Zhaoxiang, the squad leader of the 4th District Detective Squad of the Water Police, was sentenced to seven years in prison by the Shanghai District Court for beating boatman Lu A'gen to death. Zhang appealed to the High Court, which has already completed the hearing. Yesterday (the 12th), the verdict was still seven years of imprisonment.

Changshu

Three Boats Robbed in Donghu: Donghu in this county was originally an important transportation route, but reeds grow densely, making it easy for bandits to hide. The night before last, a merchant ship was passing by when it was suddenly intercepted by two bandit boats. They robbed the ship for more than ten minutes before leaving. After a while, Gu A'er's yellow mud boat was passing by and was spotted by the bandits, who fired a shot to stop it. As a result, several hundred copper coins were robbed. Later, a civilian boat from Kunshan with five passengers, including the employer He Rongrong, was spotted by the bandits. They fired a shot, breaking the glass window but fortunately not injuring anyone. He saw this and immediately ordered the boat to stop. Seven or eight people rushed forward and robbed silver, clothes, and other items worth about a hundred yuan. He, seeing the robbery, shouted for the police. The bandits became enraged and fired their guns. He was hit by a stray bullet in the leg. At that time, blood flowed like a river, but fortunately, the bone was not injured, so there was no major problem.

Rumor of County Magistrate Tan's Transfer to Qingpu: County Magistrate Tan Yigui of this county has been in office for more than a year. According to private sources in Zhenjiang, the Department of Civil Affairs plans to transfer Tan to Qingpu, and the vacant position will be filled by Yu Ding, the former county magistrate of Qingpu. County Magistrate Tan has asked for leave to go to the province. It is unknown if he will be transferred or not.

Provincial Representative Election Fails: The county party department's re-election of provincial representatives was originally scheduled for August 1st. However, due to a sudden case of peritonitis in the provincial supervisor Chen Kanghe, it could not be held. The province then sent Sun Danchen to Changshu and set the re-election for 9:00 AM on the 9th. To everyone's surprise, less than half of the attendees were present at the time (there were originally twenty candidates for representatives, but only ten were present on the day), and the meeting was declared a failure. Supervisor Sun left Changshu in the afternoon and reported the complex reasons for the failure to produce a provincial representative to the provincial party. On the 10th, Wu Zhongying and Shen Zuguan, the two party members here, also went to the province to make a statement.

Increased Defense Forces Continue to Arrive in Changshu: The 2nd Battalion of the 1st Regiment of the Provincial Security Force has been stationed in Changshu for three months. Due to the unrest among bandits in the four townships, the companies have been stationed in Hupu and Taicang Floating Bridge. The 5th Company of the battalion is still stationed at the Jiangyin Corps Headquarters. Battalion Commander Shen here, due to the insufficient number of soldiers in the battalion headquarters, has been approved by the corps headquarters to transfer the 5th Company to Changshu to increase the city's defense strength. The company departed from Jiangyin on foot on the 8th and stayed overnight in Yangku. The next day, they arrived in Changshu and were assigned by the battalion headquarters to stay in the Boruo Temple outside the North Gate.

Tax Collectors Accused of Embezzling Grain: County tax collectors Wu et al. have embezzled about 100,000 yuan of grain over the years. Xu Zhenggang and others have obtained solid evidence and petitioned the county government to recover the funds. They received a written reply, ordering the Finance Bureau to investigate and report. Xu and others claim that Wang Huazhao, the former Director of the Finance Bureau, delayed the report and repeatedly urged him to no avail. They have jointly petitioned the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Finance to send personnel to investigate.

Trial Opens in Lawsuit Against Police Officer for Neglect of Duty: Lu Zhilin, a police officer at the 3rd Branch Station of the Zhaotunqiao Public Security Bureau in the 7th District of the county, was sued by Zhou Junren, the recent patrol captain, for accepting bribes from gambling dens and abusing civil and criminal cases. The county government approved the lawsuit and summoned the plaintiff and defendant to court. The National Judge presided over the interrogation. The two sides argued fiercely. As a result, the court ordered the defendant Police Officer Lu to provide a security deposit of 2,000 yuan and await investigation.

Wuxi

The Minister of Military Affairs Visits Wuxi The Vice Minister and Acting Minister of the Military Affairs Department of the National Government, Chen Yi, went to the Suhu area the day before yesterday to handle important official matters and inspect the garrison troops. He then took a train to Wuxi from Shanghai at 9:00 am yesterday. After Minister Chen got off the train, he went to the headquarters of the First Regiment of the Military Police to inspect for a week. He then went to the railway hotel to rest. At 1:00 pm, he took a car to Meiyuan to visit the scenic spots. At about 4:00 pm, he took a car back to Nanjing.

The Department Orders the Dissolution of the General Office of Trade Unions The General Office of Trade Unions in this county recently submitted its organizational charter to the county government for approval. County Magistrate Chen forwarded it to the Department of Construction for approval. After receiving the report, Director Sun issued an order yesterday stating that the organization of the General Office of Trade Unions in various industries is not legally based and should be dissolved. A report should be submitted on the implementation of this order.

Explanation of Key Points of the Provisional Court The county government recently received a provincial order to establish a special court to hear counter-revolutionary cases. The Jiangsu Higher Court recently submitted a request to the Ministry of Justice for an interpretation of two points regarding the provisional court: whether judicial officers should wear uniforms and whether lawyers should be allowed to appear in court to defend the accused. The instructions from the Ministry of Justice have been received: (1) Judicial officers under Article 7 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic of China should be assigned to appear in court in accordance with Article 5 of the Implementing Regulations of the Revised Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic of China. Except for the judges of the local court, there is no need to wear uniforms. (2) The provisional court mentioned in Article 7 of the Emergency Law for the Punishment of Acts Endangering the Republic of China is different from the previous special criminal provisional court in terms of organization, location, and reasons for its establishment. Furthermore, lawyers are only allowed to practice in ordinary courts in accordance with Article 1 of the Lawyers' Regulations. They are only allowed to practice in special judicial organs when there are special regulations. Currently, there are no special regulations allowing lawyers to appear in court in cases heard by the provisional court, so they are not allowed to defend the accused. President Lin issued an order yesterday to the county court and the county government to comply.

A Murderous Drama at the Wuxi Grand Theater The Wuxi Grand Theater in the park has been very popular since its opening. However, after 8:00 pm the night before last, more than 30 people in naval police uniforms suddenly rushed in. The ticket sellers tried to stop them, leading to a conflict. In the chaos, they used their belts and benches as weapons, causing the ticket sellers Xue Guangtao and Yu Agen to be injured and bleeding. Many objects were also destroyed. Afterwards, the police officers dispersed. The theater found a military cap and a belt on the ground. Along with the injured Xue Guangtao and Yu Agen, they were sent to the county court for examination and then to the hospital for treatment. They also filed a lawsuit with the court to punish the perpetrators and compensate for the losses.

Changzhou

Poisonous Substances Seized at Benniu Station A large quantity of poisonous substances was discovered at Benniu Station in Wuyi on the morning of the 10th. The Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau and the Water Police Merchant Corps went to investigate and retrieve the substances, which included two boxes of sugar powder, weighing a total of 101 kilograms, and one box of morphine extract, weighing approximately 40 kilograms. However, this was less than the amount stated on the shipping manifest. The station has dispatched police officers to guard the substances.

Zhenjiang

Rice Industry Voluntarily Suppresses Rice Prices Recently, droughts have affected various provinces. Rice prices in Zhenjiang have been rising daily due to the gradual scarcity of sources, reaching 15 yuan per dan (unit of dry measure). The rice shops do not have sufficient stock. At this time between harvests, the market price is expected to increase further. The Rice Industry Association convened a meeting of merchants yesterday for the sake of maintaining the people's food supply. It was decided that the highest market price for high-quality white rice should not exceed 15 yuan, and all merchants were notified to comply and not to increase prices privately.

The Grand Canal Embankment is Under Pressure Recently, the water level of the Grand Canal in Jiangbei has risen sharply. Sun Hongzhe, Director of the Department of Construction, led Pei Yixiang, Chief Engineer of the Water Conservancy Bureau, on a second inspection tour. They returned to the province by boat last night. It is reported that the water conditions were turbulent along the upper and lower reaches of the Zhou Canal. In addition, the Yi River flooded, and the water level rose by more than one zhang (unit of length) in seven days. The eastern embankment of the Grand Canal is in danger. Among the counties along the canal, Huai'an County has made great efforts in rescue and protection, and the embankment within its jurisdiction is relatively stable. The upper reaches of the Grand Canal are increasingly urgent due to the flooding of the Yi River. Director Mao of the Water Conservancy Bureau has personally gone to Qingjiangpu to oversee the work. He departed from Gaoyou the night before last (the 10th). Pei, Chief Engineer, also went to Gaoyou to oversee the work, departing from Zhenjiang at 4:00 am yesterday (the 12th). The canal embankment stretches for more than 300 li (unit of distance), and it is now planned to raise it by 5 chi (unit of length). The Water Conservancy Bureau is dispatching a large number of surveyors to measure and stake the embankment, and construction will begin immediately.

Merger of Cotton Mills in Nantong, Hai'an, and Qidong The Dasheng Cotton Mill in Tangzha, Nantong, the Jiangjiaqiao Branch Mill, the Changlezhen Cotton Mill in Hai'an, and the Jiulongzhen Cotton Mill in Qidong are about to merge. Profits and losses will be shared, and mutual maintenance will be provided. Directors and supervisors from each factory have come to Nantong to discuss the details.

County Government Concludes Long-Pending Bandit Case The bandit case detained by the county government has been pending for more than two months due to the issue of jurisdiction. A joint order has now been received from the Pacification Office of the Provincial Government to submit the interrogation of the bandits to the Provincial Government for review. All Red bandits will be transferred to the Provincial Provisional Military Tribunal in Zhenjiang for interrogation.

Chamber of Commerce Advises Against Unauthorized Price Increases in Various Industries Due to the recent stationing of troops in Tongcheng, stores have occasionally deliberately raised prices. Jiangyin

Headquarters Captures Extortionist Zhu Mian, the commander of the Jiangxi and Zhejiang provinces' Taihu bandit suppression, received an extortion letter last month demanding 600 yuan. On the 9th, he received a letter from the local post office urging him to pay, setting a deadline of 7:15 pm today, with the money to be placed along the Hongqiao Riverbank, behind the back gate of Nanjin School. On this day, Commander Zhu followed the instructions and placed 600 yuan in banknotes, wrapped in newspaper, at the designated location. At about 7:00 pm, adjutant Zhu Zhao and special agent Cao, disguised as people from Jiangbei, waited by boat at the entrance of the Education Bureau. At 7:30 pm, they saw a person pacing and observing the area. The person went to the destination, picked up the money, and Adjutant Zhu went ashore and captured him. He was taken to the security regiment headquarters at the Guan Yue Temple, where Commander Zhu interrogated him. The person confessed to being Shen Bingzhang, courtesy name Yi Zhi, nickname A Zhang, 20 years old, son of Jin Shou and brother of Chu Zhang, a teacher at Fu Yan. He lived west of the Wenheng Bridge and was a soldier on the Buxian patrol ship. He recently took leave to go home due to beriberi. He admitted to writing the extortion letter as a joke. His handwriting also seemed to match. In the afternoon, Commander Zhu and Adjutant Zhu went to Shen's house to investigate and inquired about Shen's usual behavior from his neighbors. They learned that Sun Baocheng's family, Xiecheng Village, and Zhang Sunyi's family, diagonally across from his house, had also received extortion letters. Zhang Wenqing's family in Zhongjie had received two letters. Commander Zhu believed that the repeated occurrence of this incident in the urban area was a matter of public safety. At about 5:00 pm, he sent Shen to the county government, where County Magistrate Peng personally interrogated him. Shen firmly denied the writing on the letter, but his handwriting matched the extortion letter. After the interrogation, Adjutant Zhu escorted him back to the regiment headquarters to await further investigation.

Debate Over Whether to Open the Zhaoguan Dam Due to the continuous southeast winds, the water level of the moat in Yangzhou has risen sharply. As of the 11th, the Zhaoguan Three Ditch Sluice Gate of Jiangdu Pan still had 2 zhang and 4 chi and 1 cun (unit of length). However, the people upstream saw that the Xinnan Dam was not discharging smoothly and telegraphed the province, begging to open the Zhaoguan Dam. The people downstream desperately protected the dam. Dai Tianqiu and others here, in view of the history of the Zhaoguan Dam, not only because the stone work was damaged and difficult to repair and block, but also because the opening of the Zhaoguan Dam would turn the counties downstream into fish and turtles, telegraphed the provincial government, saying, "The Zhaoguan Dam is only a name, and it will never be opened. This has long been decided. Please do not lightly listen to the demands of a few people upstream and cause the deaths of millions of people in the counties downstream. Dai Tianqiu, etc. of Jiangdu kowtow."

Zhenjiang News Two hundred people from the five counties of Yancheng, Funing, Taixian, Dongtai, and Xinghua in the province went to the provincial government yesterday morning to petition. Gaoyou

Three People Caught Stealing and Digging Embankment The Xiejia Embankment in the southern township of this county has more than 100,000 mu (unit of area) of farmland. Recently, the embankment has been in danger of collapsing due to erosion by the dam water. Farmers inside the embankment have been guarding against danger day and night. However, at about 12:00 last night (the 8th), the farmers guarding against danger suddenly saw someone stealing and digging the embankment. They immediately sounded the gong to gather the crowd and chased down two men and one woman. They also found an iron shovel. The three were sent to the Guangyuan Township Office. After interrogation by Township Head Chen, they confessed to being instructed by someone. When asked who instructed them, they refused to tell the truth. Township Head Chen believed that the matter concerned the lives and property of the entire embankment and planned to send the three criminals to the county government to request severe punishment.

Refugees Fleeing Famine Robbed En Route More than ten refugees fleeing famine to the south were loaded onto a boat in Youlin the day before yesterday. When they arrived at Baimamiao, they were suddenly met by four soldiers and bandits, each holding a handgun, who ordered them to stop. They swarmed onto the boat and robbed all the refugees of their travel expenses. Afterwards, the refugees had no travel expenses to go south and begged the boat owner to take them back to Youlin.

Ningbo

Yu Dengji Kidnapped in Yuyao Yu Liancai of Tanhai Village, Yuyao, had worked in the salt fields for many years and had a comfortable life. His only son, Dengji, had been a senior clerk in the salt affairs agency and had a good monthly income. Dengji recently fell ill and was bedridden, in serious condition. At 11:00 pm on the 6th, six bandits suddenly arrived, carrying pistols and acting fiercely. They broke into the upstairs room and forcibly dragged Dengji away, kidnapping him to the northwest. More than 200 yuan worth of cash and clothes were robbed. Before leaving, they sent a letter demanding a ransom, inviting the family to prepare silver and go to Shanghai to redeem the ticket.

Two Kidnappings (1) Wang Shuibao, a resident of Yunjiangqiao Yuncun Village, Yin County, was a farmer. At about 3:00 am the day before yesterday, nine bandits suddenly arrived, carrying weapons, and broke in over the wall. Wang Shuibao heard the alarm and got out of bed, but was unable to escape and was kidnapped by the bandits. His whereabouts are still unknown. (2) Li Ahua, a resident behind the Xie Xinglong Nanhuo Store at Haiyan Temple, Yuyao, was quite wealthy. He had previously received an extortion letter demanding 30,000 yuan, which Li ignored. At midnight yesterday, four or five bandits suddenly arrived, carrying wooden shells, broke into the room, and kidnapped Li Ahua. Li was already over sixty years old, and his family was very anxious after the kidnapping.

Bandit Commits Suicide by Jumping into the Sea Liu Xueliang and Lu Zongdao, the leaders of the bandits in Dinghai, organized the Loyalty Society in Shenjiamen, recruiting hooligans and bandits, endangering the local area. The Provincial Anti-Banditry Bureau secretly ordered the Water Police Bureau to arrest them. After receiving the order, Wang Wenlun, the director of the Water Police Bureau, personally went to investigate and arrest them on the Taian warship yesterday. Upon arriving at Shenjiamen, he learned that the criminals had fled to Putuo. Director Wang, together with Huang Qijia, the first water patrolman, and Wang Yonghua, the director of the Shenjiamen Public Security Bureau, went to Putuo Mountain. They found the bandit leader Lu Zongdao in the Miyan Temple on the mountain and arrested him. He was taken to the Taian warship and guarded by the police. Unexpectedly, the criminal pretended to go to the toilet and jumped into the sea. By the time the guard reported to the captain, the criminal was gone. Also, four policemen from the Zhenhai County Public Security Bureau, Kong Shiyuan and others, were ordered by the county government at 1:00 pm the day before yesterday to escort the four criminals Jin A'er, Hu A'fu, Zhang A'fa, and Shen Chuangui to the Dinghai County Court for interrogation on the Yaozhao ship. When the ship sailed to the sea area of Damiaoshan in Dingshu, the two criminals Zhang A'fa and Shen Chuangui pretended to go to the toilet and took the opportunity to jump into the sea. The criminals' hands and feet were shackled, and they sank very quickly. By the time the ship stopped to rescue them, it was too late.

Education News

Important News

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education

Orders to the Education Bureaus of Songjiang and Jiangdu Counties

Regarding the Budget for the 20th Year

Order to Songjiang Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education Instruction No. 7171 to Songjiang County Education Bureau: The report is acknowledged. The increased education fees in various counties were originally intended to expand undertakings. Since the increase in education fees in this county in the 16th year, the class fees of various schools have increased sharply. The advanced funding for each grade of the complete primary school has reached an average of more than 1,300 yuan. With such high budget standards, the funding is insufficient, and it is difficult to expand the undertakings, which defeats the original purpose of increasing education fees. In order to promote the popularization of education and increase economic efficiency in various counties, the department believes that more undertakings can be managed with fewer funds. Therefore, last year, after careful consideration, a standard was formulated and ordered to be followed. Now, other counties have complied. Even a few counties that feel difficult and need to make slight changes have made considerable reductions. Only this county argues that it is difficult to reduce because it is near Shanghai. The department then ordered it to follow the methods of Baoshan and other counties. However, the director of the bureau still requested that the reduction be made gradually over the years. Therefore, the reduction in the budget for the 19th year was minimal. When the budget for the 20th year was submitted to the department, it was reviewed in detail and slightly reduced leniently, in the hope of gradually reducing it. However, the schools repeatedly requested to maintain the budget amount for the 17th year. The department had no choice but to send a special commissioner to investigate the actual situation. The commissioner found that the cost of living in the county was lower than in Shanghai and no different from other neighboring counties. However, the class fee for primary schools exceeded the department's standard by more than 400 yuan for advanced grades and more than 40 yuan for elementary grades. The commissioner's proposed reduction, taking into account the county's economic situation, was appropriate. The original report failed to consider the overall situation. The department's standard is 350 yuan per year for each elementary grade and 700 yuan per year for each advanced grade. If expenses can be reduced and redundant staff eliminated, then each elementary grade with one teacher can not only pay a monthly salary of more than 20 yuan but also have dozens of yuan for miscellaneous expenses. Each advanced grade is calculated with one and a half teachers. Except for schools with only one advanced grade, each person can be paid an average monthly salary of 30 yuan. The annual salary for each grade is only 540 yuan, leaving 160 yuan for miscellaneous expenses. Although the treatment is not very high, it is not as bad as the original report claims. According to the county's current class fee standard, the average annual expenditure for each advanced grade is more than 1,100 yuan. Calculated with one and a half teachers, the monthly salary of each teacher is more than 30 yuan, reaching 40 to 50 yuan, which is too high. Even the ordinary primary school class fees in counties near Shanghai are not known to be so high. The director of the bureau, who is responsible for the county's education administration, did not investigate the methods of neighboring counties and did not earnestly advise the schools on their requests. Instead, he simply forwarded the requests with the words "still the actual situation," maintaining the original plan, which is irresponsible. The director is ordered to follow the instructions in Instructions Nos. 1236 and handle the matter properly. If it is considered difficult to reduce the fees suddenly, a plan should be drafted, referring to the methods of neighboring counties and the situation of local schools, and submitted for approval for selection. This order is also to be followed.

Order to Jiangdu The education budget for Jiangdu for the 20th year has been repeatedly reduced by the department and the county. Now, there are still some points in the original budget that need to be revised. The department orders the county to instruct the bureau to follow the following: "The submitted documents have been acknowledged. The submitted education budget and the plan previously sent by the county education bureau are generally consistent. However, there are still some points that need to be revised, which are listed separately on the left: (1) The county junior high school actually has nine grades of students, but the budget only lists funding for seven grades. The remaining two grades are self-sufficient with tuition fees. This method is inappropriate. Now that there is no way to increase funding, the grades should be gradually reduced to a maximum of six grades. (2) The number of mu donations listed in the two separate books of the Yi Society and the She Society are each short. What exactly are they used for? A detailed explanation should be submitted immediately, and the shortage should be made up to emphasize special funds. (3) The county's education fees are heavily in arrears. In addition to the bureau's efforts to save on extravagant expenses, it should also find ways to rectify income and open up sources. The accumulation of malpractices in collection should be discussed with the county magistrate, and the finance bureau should be urged to find ways to eliminate them as soon as possible. (4) The part about primary school rectification should be handled in accordance with the report of Inspector Yang. (5) The organizational methods of the Education Endowment Management Committee should be revised in accordance with the report of Inspector Yang. (6) The expenses for the simplified elementary schools in the compulsory education pilot area have not been included in the budget, which is inappropriate and should be added immediately, and a plan and budget should be submitted for approval. (7) The county's literacy movement propaganda committee was established on April 9 this year. Why is the establishment of the committee still listed? Is it a mistake in guiding the establishment of district branches and township branches? An explanation should be submitted. (8) The county's mobile library and mobile lecture group were previously ordered not to be established separately. Why have they not been followed? The amounts for the expenses of these two times in the original budget should be deleted first. The Public Education Hall and the Public Lecture Hall should separately draft and submit a plan budget for approval. Before approval, no expenses may be used. If there are any unauthorized expenses, the director of the bureau shall be responsible for compensation. This order is to be followed, and the remaining are approved for implementation as planned. The mu donation expenditure book for the 20th year should be submitted for issuance in two semesters after the schools open. A copy of the original budget is returned, and the bureau is instructed to delete and retain it for reference."

Zhejiang Province

Seventeen Education Bureau Directors Registered

Interview and Discussion Today

The Zhejiang Provincial Department of Education, in order to publicly select talents and increase the effectiveness of education undertakings, held a registration for education bureau directors. This Port

Municipal Xinlu Normal School After Reorganization

Since Director Xu took office, the Municipal Education Bureau has been striving to improve education in the city. He deeply knows that to develop primary school education, it is necessary to start with training teachers. Therefore, the former Municipal Rural Normal School has been expanded and renamed Xinlu Normal School with the approval of the Municipal Government. Two groups of agricultural and industrial arts have been added to train teachers for the work subjects of various primary schools. Now, the old school buildings are insufficient, and classrooms, dormitories, workshops, etc. have been added. They will soon be completed, and a large number of instruments have been purchased to complete the equipment. Zhong Shijie, who is also the principal, has planned the school affairs for the next semester in detail. It is reported that the teachers have in-depth research on normal education and specialized subjects. Therefore, those who applied for the entrance examination this time are very enthusiastic.

First Class 108 Schools... Second Class 136 Schools

The fourth inspection of Party Ideology Education in primary and secondary schools by the Training Department of the Shanghai Municipal Party Committee has been completed, except for the results of the secondary school part, which have been announced earlier. Mr. Zhou Tianchong Returns Home After Completing His Studies

Mr. Zhou Tianchong went to France to study in 1928, majoring in history at the University of Paris. He specialized in the study of modern history of Western countries. After obtaining a master's degree from the University of Paris in 1929, he was guided by Professor Seignobos, director of modern history at the University of Paris (Mr. Seignobos is nearly 80 years old this year, has written extensively, and is a leader in the French history community), to prepare for a doctorate. His research paper, "The Irish Independence Movement," was passed at the University of Paris this summer and was greatly appreciated by Professor Seignobos, Professor Norovan (professor of European war history at the University of Paris), and Professor Pashes, professor of modern French history at the University of Paris. What attracted the attention of French historians to Mr. Zhou's thesis was the discovery of a secret agreement between the Irish revolutionaries and Germany in 1916 to jointly attack England. Before going abroad, Mr. Zhou studied education and wrote extensively. No one in the domestic education community does not know his name. It is reported that Mr. Zhou returned to China from France on August 7 and will engage in writing and translation in order to make contributions to history.

Local News

Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs

Suppressing the Soaring Rice Prices

Top-Quality Rice Fixed at 18 Yuan and 9 Jiao Starting Today

Prices Must Return to the Original Limit Within a Week

Strictly Prohibiting Black Market Trading, Severe Punishment After Investigation

Rice prices have been soaring for days, causing public panic and uncertainty. The price on the 11th of this month reached 19 yuan and 5 jiao for top-quality rice. Yesterday (the 12th), the number of rice shipments arriving from the north and south of the city was scarce, and the storage in the river was even more lacking. The market atmosphere became even stronger, with a trend of rising by 7 or 8 jiao. Mr. Feng Liutang, the section chief of the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, rushed to the North Market Rice Exchange Office in Xinzha at 8 AM yesterday to order a temporary suspension of price increases. He immediately convened rice merchants, distributors, and boatmen from Changzhou and Xichang at the office to analyze the causes of the price increase, which were approximately as follows: (1) Reports of floods from various places have caused more panic, and many are buying relief rice. In recent days, a large amount of rice has been transported westward from Wuxi and other places. (2) It is generally known that rice storage in various places is still abundant this year, and more than 400,000 bags of foreign rice have been scheduled to arrive, of which more than 300,000 bags have already been sold out. There is no confirmed date for the arrival of the remaining rice. (3) The amount of rice stored in various warehouses in this city is less than at this time last year. Due to the expectation of a bumper harvest last autumn, everyone dared not hoard it, resulting in a lack of rice to supply when the source is scarce. (4) The floods in the interior have not completely receded. In Kunshan and Dingli, civilians are still guarding the dikes, not only obstructing the navigation of small vessels, but also prohibiting heavily loaded civilian boats from traveling with gongs. As a result, fewer rice shipments arrive by river. (5) The recent hurricane has caused rice boats on the Huangpu River to stop in port to avoid the wind, delaying their arrival in Shanghai. (6) The rice boats from various production areas initially reduced their shipments because the loading was light, and most of them went ashore to paint. The number of rice boats has decreased, and transportation by train cannot meet the demand, resulting in a scarcer source. (7) People are uneasy and generally believe that the floods and famine in various places are significant. Most households want to purchase and store rice for future needs. The supply has decreased, while the demand has increased. Rice shops are also competing to purchase goods from dealers, and boatmen are becoming more reluctant to sell, creating the current situation. In fact, rice storage in various places is still abundant, enough to meet the needs before the new rice comes out. There is no need to alarm each other and increase the price of rice, only to suffer the consequences. Moreover, the 17 yuan limit price set by the Bean and Rice Industry Association is indeed a fair price. Unexpectedly, this special situation has made it impossible to maintain the limit price. However, this change will be restored when the wind stops and the water recedes. It is a temporary phenomenon and not a cause for concern. As long as the public remains calm, the arrogance of speculators can be suppressed. However, black market trading is the biggest problem in the rice market, which is most likely to disrupt the market and raise prices. It should be eliminated as soon as possible, and then the market can return to normal. After Section Chief Feng explained the situation to everyone from various aspects, Mr. Qiang Zisheng and Jiang Shizhi also made a statement. It was then summarized into four points: (1) Strictly prohibit black market trading and make the market open. If there is any black market price gouging, the Bureau of Social Affairs will send personnel to investigate secretly at any time, and each trade association will be responsible for reporting. Once verified, severe penalties will be imposed. (2) The price of 17 yuan should be the principle, but in this state of wind and water disaster, the price of rice has actually reached more than 20 yuan. Top-quality japonica rice is temporarily allowed to be priced at a maximum of 18 yuan and 9 jiao, and medium and inferior rice should be priced accordingly. It is only allowed to fall, not to rise. The time limit is one week, falling back to the maximum price of 17 yuan per stone. (3) Arriving good rice should be fairly distributed by the trade, and no price gouging should be allowed. When rice shops purchase large quantities, they should be dissuaded immediately. (4) The Bureau of Social Affairs should forward a letter to the Railway Bureau to allocate more vehicles to transport rice to Shanghai. Rice shops and rice dealers should also limit prices in order to benefit the people. The whole body agreed and promised to abide by it and not change it. The meeting adjourned at 12 o'clock. The North Market also opened immediately. However, the South Market did not have time to open because it was already late when the North Market made its decision. The Bureau of Social Affairs has already written to the Railway Administration Bureau, forwarding it to the rice stations along the route, requesting that they try to allocate more vehicles to facilitate the transportation of rice to Shanghai to help the people's food supply in this city. Food households in this city should also remain calm and not rush to accumulate rice, which will cause price increases. It is expected that the price will soon return to its previous level.

Xu Shiying Hosted Financial Circles Yesterday

Discussing Salt Tax Treasury Bonds

Substantial Results Have Been Achieved

Since Mr. Xu Shiying, chairman of the Relief Commission, received 2 million yuan in salt tax treasury bonds from the Ministry of Finance to address the flood disasters in various provinces, he believed that the disaster situation was serious and that relief should be distributed immediately. Therefore, at 12 noon yesterday, he hosted a banquet at the Hong Kong Road Banking Club, inviting important figures from the banking circles in Shanghai. During the banquet, Mr. Xu Shiying, chairman of the Relief Commission, reported on the detailed disaster situation and the current situation of the disaster victims in various provinces, requesting the gentlemen in the banking circles in Shanghai to raise 1 million yuan in advance to distribute emergency relief, using the 2 million yuan in salt tax treasury bonds issued by the Ministry of Finance as collateral. After discussion among the representatives of the banking and financial industries, it was agreed that the banking industry would be responsible for allocating 700,000 yuan, and the financial industry would be responsible for allocating 300,000 yuan, with a minimum interest rate of 7 per mille per month, to be paid in full immediately in order to rush the emergency relief. The amount of debt assumed by the banking industry totaled 700,000 yuan, which was determined on the spot. The Central Bank accounted for 100,000 yuan, the Bank of China 100,000 yuan, the Bank of Communications 50,000 yuan, the Shanghai Bank 50,000 yuan, the Jin Cheng Bank 50,000 yuan, the Zhongnan Bank 50,000 yuan, the Salt Industry Bank 30,000 yuan, the Continental Bank 30,000 yuan, the Four Banks Reserve 50,000 yuan, the Zhejiang Industrial Bank 30,000 yuan, the Xingye Bank 30,000 yuan, the China Industrial Bank 30,000 yuan, the Si Ming Bank 30,000 yuan, the Kenye Bank 30,000 yuan, the Guohua Bank 30,000 yuan, and the Commercial Bank 10,000 yuan. Mr. Qian Runqing, a leader in the financial industry, was responsible for the 300,000 yuan assumed by the financial industry, which would be allocated among more than 70 money shops in Shanghai according to their capacity.

China-Japan Agreement Research Association

Letter Requesting Collection of Opinions from Various Industries

The Committee for the Study of Sino-Japanese Agreement Tariffs sent a letter to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce and the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating: "Dear Sirs, We have investigated the Sino-Japanese Agreement and found that the tariffs levied by both sides are extremely unequal. Therefore, Chinese goods shipped to Japan and Korea have plummeted, which is equivalent to being cut off, compared to the long drive and irresistible momentum of Japanese goods. The difference between the two is really immeasurable. In order to prepare for the worst and save the declining trend, our association has specially submitted a request to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting that the public be allowed to participate in the opinions. Soon, we received a telegram from the Ministry, ordering our association to convene relevant groups, carefully discuss, and study the results, and submit them to the Ministry for adoption, etc. Upon receiving this order, our association invited relevant groups to hold a joint meeting on June 23 of this year, and publicly elected 13 groups as members to form the Committee for the Study of Sino-Japanese Agreement Tariffs. Then, on the 5th of this month, we held the inaugural meeting, and each member took the oath of office, and decided on the procedures for the meeting. However, we have found that the number of our country's goods sold to Japan and Korea in the past was very large. Since Japan has repeatedly increased our import tariffs to the point of extracting 100%, they have been completely cut off, and it is difficult to sell even an inch of goods. Although the Sino-Japanese Agreement signed by our country's government and the Japanese side has reduced the tax by 30%, the tax rate of 70% is still too far from the tax rate levied on Japanese goods shipped to Korea and shipped to China, which is equivalent to zero. Therefore, revising this agreement is the only urgent task of our country's industrial and commercial circles. Moreover, the term of the agreement is three years, and now it is more than a year since the agreement was signed, and there is only one year of hesitation time. The contract will expire soon, and it is urgent to collect opinions from various industries and relevant associations as much as possible on the revision of the tariff in the Sino-Japanese Agreement, compile and review them, study them in detail, and invite legal and tariff experts to participate in the work, and then summarize them and compile a proposal to submit to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for adoption and implementation, and to propose to Japan to revise the contract at the expiration date, in order to save the dying industry and commerce and benefit the development of national goods. It has been decided by the inaugural meeting and the first committee meeting of our association to request the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to send a letter to each trade association, requesting them to quickly collect the opinions of various industries on the revision of the tariff in the Sino-Japanese Agreement, compile them and submit them to our association for research and review, and submit them to the Ministry for adoption. We have the honor to present this matter to you, and we implore your association to quickly send a letter to each trade association, collect their opinions on the revision of the tariff in the Sino-Japanese Agreement, compile them and submit them to our association, so that we can proceed. We are extremely grateful for your attention."

Anti-Japanese Association Carefully Employs Staff

Must Obtain Guarantees from Two or More Committee Members

If There is Any Embezzlement or Malpractice, They Should Be Subject to the Same Punishment

The Anti-Japanese Aid Overseas Chinese Committee, in view of the unsatisfactory performance of the previous Anti-Japanese Association, and the key lies in the fact that on the one hand, the chairman system was adopted, and on the other hand, the employment of staff was not cautious enough. Therefore, at the beginning of its establishment, the chairman system was changed to a standing committee system. All release of goods, detention of goods, and important daily affairs must be agreed upon by four or more standing committee members before they can be exercised. Standing committee meetings are held three times a week to avoid delays. As for the staff of the association, it is often decided by the standing committee meeting that they must obtain the introduction and guarantee of two or more executive committee members. The guarantee must state that if there is any malpractice in the future, they are willing to be subject to the same punishment. The regulations are extremely strict.

Customs Brokerage Industry

Please Abolish Foreign Customs Brokerage Firms

Recommend Chairman Shi Zhikun to Petition in Beijing

The Shanghai Transit Customs Brokerage Association, in view of the prevalence of foreign customs brokerage firms, which damages national rights and commerce, has recommended the association's chairman, Shi Zhikun, to go to Beijing to petition the Executive Yuan and the Ministries of Finance and Foreign Affairs. Mr. Shi has already taken the night express train to Beijing last night. The text of his petition is recorded as follows: "A petition is hereby submitted stating that foreigners are privately setting up customs brokerage firms, taking care of national taxes, infringing upon customs rights, and requesting that the Jianghai Customs investigate and revoke their licenses in order to maintain the national system and safeguard commerce. Tracing back to the loss of control of the Qing government, and foreign insults relying upon, the disaster of decline, has reached today. Due to the customs tariff agreement, the path of domestic production and industry will never be revitalized. Due to the division of customs rights, the possibility of prohibiting military contraband products from abroad is almost non-existent. And the Japanese are particularly dangerous and their plans are particularly skillful. They are even privately organizing customs brokerage firms in our country, registering with the customs, and taking care of customs taxes. The customs personnel have no national knowledge and think that customs clearance and tax payment are just one type of commercial behavior, and they are not careful and allow them to set up. How can they know that the international customs regulations are heavily guarded? Customs clearance and tax payment are extremely restrictive. If Chinese people are engaged in this industry, they must provide security deposits and set up joint guarantees, let alone foreigners. Even the most preferential agreements will never allow it. The rights of the country are related, and the principle should be like this. However, foreigners despise sovereignty and openly operate tax returns in our country. This has never been recorded in previous sessions, and it is even less allowed by international commercial law. It is requested that our Minister of the Court immediately stop it. According to the behavioral capacity of corporate legal persons, it is stipulated in the domestic law that foreign commercial offices in China are subject to the restrictions stipulated in the domestic law, and registration with the competent authority is a prerequisite. Foreign customs brokerage firms infringe upon customs rights, and the facts are obvious. The customs supervisor, as a Chinese person, should have no reason to rashly register them. If they are not registered, then all commercial activities of foreign customs brokerage firms are invalid. I am sincerely afraid that the customs officers will be ignorant and register them directly, and the foreigners will use this as a basis, rely on the consul for protection, rely on their financial resources as a backing, and squeeze out the legitimate commerce in the country, leaving them with no place to stand. This is a harm to the people's livelihood. Smuggling military contraband goods to foreign countries will always breed the roots of turmoil, which will harm the country. As for leaks, frauds, and violations of national regulations, it is not within the reach of national regulations and laws, and the harm is still small. It is requested that our Minister of the Court immediately correct it. This matter concerns national rights and is related to the people's livelihood. In addition to having presented it to the Shanghai Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for review, I have specially recommended our chairman, Shi Zhikun, to bring the text and appeal to the Governor-General, ordering the Customs Administration to send a document to all customs offices to revoke the registration numbers of foreign-owned customs brokerage firms in order to consolidate national rights and safeguard commerce. We are truly in a state of waiting for orders."

Boycott of Japanese Goods in Progress

New Developments in the Cotton Textile Industry

Actively Preparing Cotton Textile Factories: Since the initiation of organizing cotton yarn factories by dyeing and weaving colleagues in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, colleagues from various places have been very enthusiastic in taking on the role of promoters. Yesterday, a joint meeting of all representatives and promoters was held again at the Ruilinli Assembly Hall on Avenue Edward VII. Dozens of people, including Zhu Wenqi, Qiu Shuqiao, Chen Liesheng, Zhu Zhenhan, Gao Ruohua, Gao Jinru, Jiang Yongsheng, Que Pingzhi, Yan Guangdi, Guan Bingqing, Pan Xusheng, Tang Fuan, and Wang Tingcun, attended. The fundamental methods for excluding Japanese goods were discussed in detail. It was unanimously agreed that the organization of a fine yarn factory could not be delayed any longer and should be actively carried out. The following resolutions were immediately made public: (1) A preparatory committee for the organization of a cotton yarn factory should be established immediately, with thirteen members. One representative should be nominated from each of the counties with the highest yarn consumption in dyeing and weaving industries outside the city, such as Wuxi, Jiangyin, Wujin, Hangzhou, Wuxian, and Changshu. One representative should be nominated from each of the cotton weaving, knitting, and mercerized silk industries in the city, and one from the towel industry. (2) The inaugural meeting of the preparatory committee will be held next Monday at 10:00 AM at the same location, the Ruilinli Assembly Hall on Avenue Edward VII.

Preparing to Be Self-Sufficient in Handkerchief Raw Materials: In the past ten years, Japan's cotton textile industry has made rapid progress, transporting and selling goods worth billions upon billions to China and India every year. The immaturity and stagnation of China's cotton textile industry are undeniable. Although there has been slight progress in recent years, besides being able to weave 16-count, 20-count, and 40-count doubled yarns, its technical capabilities are far behind in various fine cloths. It is now known that the raw materials used in China's handkerchief industry are all made of 80-count, 60-count, or 42-count single yarns. In the past, all of these were imported from England, with annual imports amounting to no less than five to six million. In the past two or three years, Japan has been trying to seize this business, and its products are already being shipped to China for competition. However, except for a small number of handkerchief factories, they have not yet gained the trust of major handkerchief factories. Since the May 3rd Massacre, Ma Shijie, the general manager of Jingxin Handkerchief Factory and a leader in the local handkerchief industry, has had a plan to weave his own raw materials, but it has not been realized due to various difficulties. This year, after the increase in import tariff rates, each bolt of this raw material is subject to an import tax of more than two taels, and the exchange rate fluctuates greatly. It is imperative to weave the raw materials domestically. Therefore, the factory is determined to proceed. In March, it installed machinery and started trial weaving. Since March, the results have been very satisfactory. Products are now available to supply the handkerchief department for its own use, and plans are underway to raise large sums of money for expansion. According to Mr. Feng, the factory's general manager, the factory plans to purchase 200 of the latest model machines to weave handkerchief raw materials exclusively to meet the needs of various handkerchief factories in China. He also welcomes visits from all circles.
