Zhang Zhijiang

Hosted the Press Yesterday Afternoon

Reporting on Pacification and National Arts

Zhang Zhijiang, the Director-General of the Jiangsu Pacification Office and the Director of the Central Guoshu (National Arts) Academy, hosted the press at the Dongya Restaurant yesterday afternoon to report on matters related to the Pacification Office and the Central Guoshu Academy. According to Zhang,

Pacification Plan: Through several months of effort, the remnant bandits have been largely eliminated. I have visited the Huai-Xu area and found the situation generally satisfactory. However, it is inevitable that scattered bandits will remain hidden among the people. These bandits hide when the troops arrive and plunder when the troops leave. Therefore, it is difficult to completely eliminate them by relying solely on military force. Therefore, the Pacification Office plans to adopt fundamental elimination measures during this six-month extension period. The second phase of the plan has now been drafted. On the one hand, troops will be used to suppress the bandits, and on the other hand, more attention will be paid to training local militias to enable them to fulfill their defense responsibilities and fundamentally eliminate the scourge of banditry. Troops may be transferred elsewhere at any time, while militias are permanently stationed. However, organization without training is difficult to defend oneself. Therefore, a long-term solution is sought. This plan has been discussed with the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and it will be implemented as soon as it is finalized, in order to create a solid and permanent self-defense capability for the people of Jiangsu Province. As for the troops, the recent floods in the Jiangbei area have caused all matters to be temporarily suspended. However, all units have been ordered to shift their full efforts to rescue and protect the dikes. As soon as the floods subside slightly, the plan will be implemented.

National Arts Fund: The promotion of national arts is a fundamental way to remedy the weakness of our nation. In the past, Zichan was criticized by Mencius for providing small favors by ferrying people across the Zhen and Wei rivers on oxcarts, because there were too many people crossing the rivers to be ferried across one by one. Our country is currently beset by natural disasters and man-made calamities, with internal and external troubles pressing in on us. Although the government and major charitable organizations are doing their best to provide relief, they can only take care of the present and have difficulty looking to the future. The people must still strive on their own. Dr. Sun Yat-sen once said that since the beginning of humanity, the struggle has never ceased. We are all in the midst of struggle. Chairman Chiang Kai-shek also said that we should treat wartime as peacetime and peacetime as wartime. In other words, our lives are a constant struggle, at all times and in all places. However, struggle must stem from the spirit, and the spirit must stem from physical strength. Only with a sound physique can there be a sound spirit, and only with a sound spirit can there be the ability to struggle. However, nothing can make physical strength stronger than national arts. National arts are China's treasure, but they have been abandoned and not used, allowing us to be trampled on by foreigners, creating all kinds of national humiliation. Recent cases such as the Wanbaoshan Incident and the case of French members of the Sino-French investigation team beating Chinese staff members show that the promotion of national arts is a cure for our nation. If the people were in this time of wars and disasters, everyone could struggle and everyone could defend themselves. If this could be understood by every household and popularized among the whole people, the whole country would become one, and how could it not be strong? Therefore, the government has established a National Arts Academy in the capital, and it is now establishing a National Arts Specialized School to train teachers and promote national arts throughout the country. It is currently in the fundraising period. This matter and the pacification work can be said to be treating both the symptoms and the root causes. Gentlemen, as leaders of the press, you have a guiding responsibility for social undertakings. I hope that you will provide full assistance in the future if you need to borrow from me. The future of the two tasks of pacification and national arts will surely benefit greatly. Yuan Yeyu of the press then gave a reply, and the meeting adjourned at around 2:00 PM.

Ratepayers Oppose Property Valuation for Donation

Reiteratingly Admonishing the Municipal Council

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association sent a letter to Mackie, the acting director of the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council, yesterday, stating, "Sir, We have received your reply No. 1098 dated July 30th regarding the method of collecting municipal donations for properties with actual rent, which still insists on destroying the good habits of the past. Upon examining the implications of the last paragraph of your reply, the Council believes that there is no room for change in this method of high property rent valuation for donation payment. However, this association believes that your Council is an autonomous organization formed by taxpayers, and absolutely does not want the Council's measures to differ from the wishes of taxpayers. Now, this association must again draw your Council's attention and cancel this distorted clause and disguised donation increase method for the following reasons: (1) The current municipal donation rate is 14% of the property rent. If there is an actual property rent that can be used as a standard for municipal donations, it should not be calculated based on the actual rent, but arbitrarily calculated based on the estimated property rent. Then, the previous increase in the donation rate, such as from 14% to 16%, is indeed superfluous. It is only necessary to increase the actual property rent by 20%. According to the increase in the donation rate, it must be agreed upon by the ratepayers, which is a legal act under the principle of autonomy implemented by the Public Concession. If the municipal donation can be based on an estimated amount that is higher than the actual property rent, then the subsequent donation increases can be entirely controlled by the Finance Department. How can taxpayers use any method to sanction it? Increasing the donation rate also increases the burden on taxpayers. Collecting donations based on a standard exceeding the actual property rent also increases the burden on taxpayers. For example, if the actual property rent is 100 taels per month, the municipal donation calculated at 14% is 14 taels. Now, the actual monthly property rent of 100 taels is estimated at 190 taels, and calculated at 14%, it is 26 taels and 6 qian. The increase in donation is essentially the same as increasing the donation rate, and it can be done at will. Can this disguised donation increase be permitted by taxpayers under the principle of autonomy? Therefore, this association must repeatedly admonish to maintain the two principles of autonomy and the rule of law. (2) When was the current land regulation established? There are written records to be relied upon, which will not be discussed in detail. What was the situation of the houses in the Public Concession at that time? As indicated by the facts, there were very few rental houses at that time, and most were self-owned and self-used. Under these circumstances, it was inevitable to adopt the British property tax system and use the method of rent valuation, because there was no actual property rent that could be used as a standard. The provisions of the land regulation were thus established, just like other laws and regulations, based on the current situation and had the same cause. If not, then after the implementation of the current land regulation, the municipal donation rate need not have changed as listed in Tables 147 to 148 of Volume 1 of Judge Feitang's report. The estimated hypothetical rent could be overestimated and still maintain the donation rates used in 1866 of 5% for foreigners and 8% for Chinese. (3) Fairness is the foundation for the existence of modern public institutions. If a certain obligation or right is to be given to or borne or enjoyed by a very small number of taxpayers, this is done under autocracy. How can an institution that claims to represent the rule of law and prides itself on being an autonomous organization formed by all taxpayers tolerate or act in this kind of unfair action? This association solemnly informs your Council that, in terms of the principles of autonomy, rule of law, and fairness, the director of the finance department should be ordered to stop this disguised donation increase method that is used to circumvent the ratepayers' right to consent. This kind of action is in fact an act of playing with words and laws, and is not upright. While processing, according to a letter from the Shanghai Chinese Chemical Industry Society, etc., "Sir, We are writing in reply to your letter No. 1098, which states that the property rents at No. 444 and No. 445 Henan Road are each 160 taels per month. The key point of this case is the fair treatment of taxpayers and the prohibition of increasing the donation rate by means of high property rent valuation. It is not a matter of whether the rent valuation is high or low. Your Council has not paid attention to the above-mentioned key points. Chong Qing Company cannot create this example. All of this increased property donation is really difficult to comply with. Corresponding protests are made," and so on. This association believes that it is very reasonable and corresponds to the letter, hoping that it will be checked and processed accordingly.

After the Weisshorn Ran Aground

Also Looted by Pirates

Distressed Crew and Passengers Arrive in Shanghai

The Jardine Matheson & Co.'s Weisshorn encountered a strong wind on the Fuzhou ocean and ran aground in Nanwan while sheltering from the wind. The ship was damaged, and the passengers were rescued. One crew member fell into the sea and died. This has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the ship was also looted by pirates after the accident, resulting in huge losses. The latest news is recorded below:

Warship Rescues Passengers: When the Weisshorn ran aground, the ship's radio had been destroyed by the wind and waves, and the motor had lost its effectiveness. The rescue signal could not be sent. The bottom of the ship had already been trapped in a hidden reef, and water was entering the hold. The ship's owner then used rockets for help. At this time, the wind was strong and the waves were high, and no ships were passing by. Fortunately, a foreign warship sailed from Xiamen Harbor and saw the distress signal. The ship immediately sailed to assist in the rescue. Because the bottom of the ship had been broken and could not be towed, the ship launched a sampan to transfer the rescued crew and passengers to the Hengsheng, which was sent to Shanghai. It has been confirmed that the Hengsheng is already on its way. If it does not arrive in Shanghai this afternoon, it will enter the port tomorrow morning.

Pirates Loot Property: The Weisshorn's place of the accident was at the foot of a sea island, which is a den for pirates. After the warship rescued the crew and passengers, the pirates launched sampans and ventured into the Weisshorn to loot the luggage and property left by the crew and passengers. Anything that could be carried was taken aboard the ship by the pirates. Amid the fierce wind and waves, they escaped fully loaded with stolen goods. By the time the warship transferred the rescued crew and passengers to the Hengsheng and returned to protect the ship, the pirates had already fled with their loot. It is reported that many valuables in the ship were looted, and the public and private losses were huge. The ship is now under the supervision of the warship to prevent further looting.

Comprador's Assistant Dies: According to the news obtained yesterday, the crew member who fell into the sea and died on the Weisshorn was not the comprador, but the comprador's assistant. His name is still under investigation. As for the details of the disaster, it will only be clear after the rescued crew members arrive in Shanghai. The bottom of the Weisshorn has been broken by the reef, and all the cabins are flooded. Fortunately, it is搁 resting on the reef, so it has not completely sunk. However, there is little hope of towing it. The Hong Kong head office has sent personnel to the site of the accident to survey whether it can be towed. A decision will be made after the surveyor returns. Most of the cargo in the cabins is soaked in seawater. There is no certainty whether some of it can be unloaded and transferred. The ship was originally planned to go to Tianjin after arriving in Shanghai from Hong Kong, so most of the cargo loaded on the ship was destined for North China. According to Shanghai shipping circles, the Weisshorn was the only ship that had an accident in the recent strong winds off the coast of Zhejiang and Fujian, which was very unfortunate for the company. The ship has peace insurance, so the company's losses are not much.

Municipal Government Reduces Municipal Expenses

Since the Municipal Land Bureau issued real estate deeds, it has collected real estate transfer taxes and municipal expenses in accordance with the usual practice. The real estate transfer tax was formerly known as deed tax, and the municipal expenses were formerly known as deed surcharges. This surcharge includes the expenses of the security corps, education fees, household registration fees, police fees, self-government fees, fire brigade expenses, the horse patrol fees of the former county magistrate's office, and the office expenses of the deed issuance office. The amount collected in each district varies. It is paid when the contract is signed. The receipt is filled out by the contract issuance office in each district. Later, the bureau believed that the amount collected in each district varied. Under the same city, the burden on the people should not be uneven. In May of the nineteenth year, it was approved to uniformly collect five yuan for every 100 yuan of the contract price. That is, whenever there is a real estate transfer, five yuan per 100 yuan of the contract price is collected for municipal expenses when the contract is signed. When the tax is paid, eight yuan per day is collected for the real estate transfer tax according to the contract price. The total amount of the contract price per hundred yuan is 13 yuan. After this reorganization, the burden on the two counties of Shanghai and Bao has been greatly reduced. Recently, in order to further reduce the burden on the people, Mayor Zhang instructed the Land Bureau to study the real estate transfer tax in this city, believing that the burden on the people was still too great, and instructed them to study the method and reduce it appropriately. After receiving the instructions, the Land Bureau immediately studied it in detail and planned to reduce the municipal expenses collected at 5% of the contract price to 1%. This 10% will still be allocated to the expenses of the contract distribution offices in each district as usual. It has been submitted to the Municipal Government and submitted to the Municipal Conference and the Construction Discussion Committee, and it has been approved according to the plan.

Entrusted with an Orphan During Father's Serious Illness, the Complaint Accuses of Seducing a Blood Relative Under Guardianship and Embezzling Guardian Property, Requesting Arrest and Punishment, and Ordering Compensation for Losses. Only one year had passed since the death of the plaintiff's mother. He left behind four orphans, all young. The plaintiff was the youngest, only nine years old. The other three brothers were all over ten years old. During his illness, the plaintiff's father knew he would not recover and was deeply concerned that his orphans would not be cared for after his death. Therefore, in the second month, he invited relatives Qu Shaoqing, cousin Xi Baoshi, aunt Ding, and second uncle Feizhang to gather at his bedside to entrust them with his affairs. The three brothers were entrusted to different guardians, and the fields and houses were divided among them, with a will established.

Yuquan Inherited Guardianship. Subsequently, it was agreed with Lord Feizhang to assume the responsibility of guardianship for the plaintiff, and a box of gold jewelry, estimated to weigh over twenty-four taels (detailed list of items attached), was gifted to the plaintiff, designated for her future dowry. All the relatives present at the time were aware of this. Therefore, after the plaintiff lost her father, she was sent by aunt Ding to be raised by Feizhang, and the gifted gold jewelry was also handed over for safekeeping. Several years passed, and unfortunately, Ding and Feizhang passed away one after another. The defendant, Yuquan, then succeeded his father and assumed the responsibility of guardianship for the plaintiff. All the guardian property thus came into his possession.

Lost Virginity at Sixteen. Unexpectedly, Yuquan intended to embezzle the property, unwilling for the plaintiff to grow up and have a family, thus depleting his funds. Therefore, when the plaintiff was sixteen and lacked knowledge, he used seductive words and alluring appearances to entice her in various ways. The plaintiff, initially understanding love, was ignorant of etiquette and fell into his trap, resulting in Yuquan destroying her virginity, becoming a lifelong blemish.

Accompanied to Suzhou for Childbirth. Extending to the eleventh month of the year before last, the plaintiff was fully pregnant. Yuquan feared that giving birth at home would alarm the neighbors. Therefore, on the twenty-sixth day of the same month, he personally accompanied the plaintiff to Suzhou, staying at the Weida Hospital under the pseudonym Mrs. Zhang. Yuquan personally wrote the application for admission for childbirth, residing in room number twenty-four to await delivery. After more than a month in the hospital, she gave birth to a son on December 19th. Yuquan, taking advantage of the plaintiff's postpartum confusion, took the baby away for foster care, and its whereabouts remain unknown to this day.

Denies Gold Jewelry Completely. After returning home after childbirth, Yuquan initially treated her as usual, but then gradually showed signs of disgust, repeatedly scolding her and eventually forcing her to leave home and seek a living on her own. The plaintiff also knew that living under someone else's roof was not a long-term solution. However, to live independently, she had to consider her finances and had no choice but to ask him to return the gifted gold jewelry. Yuquan completely denied it, claiming that the plaintiff was fabricating and extorting. The plaintiff then complained to her relatives, who were all indignant.

United Family Members in Violent Assault. Afterwards, the defendant also knew that he could not hide the truth from everyone. He then entrusted a cousin, Chengnuo, to come forward to mediate, willing to give a thousand gold to terminate the guardianship relationship. The plaintiff, because the amount was far from the gifted property, refused to agree hastily. The defendant then had evil thoughts, determined to make the plaintiff unable to live in peace. Therefore, in the first month of this year, he united family members and carried out a violent assault. Fortunately, it did not cause fatal injuries, and she was able to preserve her life.

Elaborate Response. The plaintiff, after suffering this humiliation, thought it best to avoid the situation and went from Suzhou to Shanghai, instructing a lawyer to send a letter of inquiry. Unexpectedly, the defendant responded with elaborate words, falsely claiming that the plaintiff was an abandoned child found by the plaintiff's late father by the roadside. Later, due to not abiding by family rules, she was expelled and floated outside, having illicit relations with someone and becoming pregnant, resulting in secretly giving birth at the hospital. Now, she is falsely accusing people, trying to extort money, and is extremely shameless, etc.

Fabricated False Letter from Cousin. At the same time, he fabricated a false letter in the name of cousin Baoshi and sent it to the lawyer to cover up for himself. Considering that the plaintiff is the biological daughter of the late father, Lord Juntang, the whole family knows this. How can the defendant slander her at will? If the plaintiff was indeed an abandoned child and Feizhang was not entrusted with guardianship, then why would the defendant and his late father have spared no expense in raising the plaintiff after the death of the adoptive parent? This is enough to know that it is a fabrication.

Cousin Knows the Truth. The late father gifted gold jewelry to the plaintiff during his illness, entrusting it to Feizhang for safekeeping. There were relatives present at the time who witnessed the entrustment. How can he arbitrarily deny it? Although most relatives have now passed away and cannot be questioned, fortunately, cousin Baoshi is still alive and can be asked for the truth. If he claims that Baoshi did not hear about this matter, then why would the defendant fabricate a reply in his name? This further reveals the defendant's falsehood.

Hospital's Handwritten Application. As for saying that the plaintiff became pregnant through adultery with others, if it were true, then the defendant would have to expel her for bringing shame to the family. How could he avoid suspicion and accompany her to Suzhou, take her to the hospital, and personally fill out the application form? The director of the Weida Hospital, who assisted in the delivery, witnessed this, and there is also the defendant's handwritten application left in the hospital for verification. The court should order an investigation and verify the handwriting to see if it is from the defendant's hand. It will not be difficult to clarify with one interrogation. As for fabricating Baoshi's private letter, not only is the handwriting the same as the defendant's reply, but Baoshi has also issued a letter stating this. The evidence is extremely conclusive.

Often Visited Shanghai. The defendant has been working as a lawyer in Shanghai, setting up an office on Weihaiwei Road. He often brought the plaintiff to Shanghai to stay, and everyone in the office knew this. Now he falsely accuses the plaintiff of fleeing for a long time. How can this not be contrary to the truth? He is a lawyer whose duty is to protect human rights and uphold the rule of law. How should he abide by the law and cherish himself? Yet, he disregards ethics, seduces a weak cousin under the age of sixteen under his guardianship. First, he defiles her virginity, then he embezzles her property, and finally, he fabricates a letter that causes harm to others to cover up his crimes.

Requesting Severe Punishment. In summary, the above has violated Article 240, Paragraph 1, Paragraph 2, Article 243, Paragraph 2, Article 352, Paragraph 1, and Article 224 of the Criminal Law. Therefore, according to Article 13 (location) and Article 337 of the Criminal Procedure Law, each item, Article 506, I hereby submit this complaint, requesting your court to review and approve the arrest of the defendant for trial and impose severe punishment to warn those who commit incest and destroy morality. At the same time, order the defendant to return the embezzled gold jewelry of twenty-four taels and zero, or compensate for the equivalent price of gold, so that the plaintiff has the resources to live and avoid becoming a starving corpse. From now on, she will seek refuge in a monastery, repent for the rest of her life, hoping to make up for it in the slightest, and be grateful for the boundless kindness. I also request that witnesses Xi Baoshi, Xi Chengnuo, and the director of Weida Hospital be summoned to court for questioning.

Pu Jinghong Burned

A Tragic Incident at the Singing Hall

First Went to Get a Permanent Wave

Carelessly Adding Alcohol Caused the Accident

Severe Injuries to Both Arms and Head

Tianyi Film Company at 232 Ganshidong Road in the French Concession has been busy lately producing the sound film "Spring in the Singing Hall." Yesterday evening at 8:30 PM, they were filming a scene with Fang Gu, the daughter of the singer Li Huifang, played by actress Pu Kunying. After filming two shots, the work was completed. However, as it was still early, Pu asked the photographer to take two still photos for her as a memento. Pu went to the dressing room to do her hair and makeup. At that time, the male and female actors were all in the photography studio. Outside the dressing room, only Duan Changxin was guarding the window. Suddenly, in an instant, a ball of fire started in the room. Duan was shocked and entered the room, seeing Pu Kunying burned by the fire and unconscious. He quickly used a cotton blanket to extinguish the fire. He then helped Pu out of the room and took her to Renji Hospital for treatment. It was found that Pu suffered severe burns, especially on both arms. Her head was also injured in various places. It is said that the cause of the fire was due to carelessness when adding alcohol. At the time, Pu was wearing a dark soft satin cheongsam, and her socks and leather shoes were also black. Pu Kunying, also known as Jinghong, is seventeen years old and from Shanghai. She joined Tianyi not long ago, and this was her first time on camera.

Lü Anchang's Heart is Too Cruel

Dug Out His Wife's Eyes

Quarreled Yesterday Morning Over a Trivial Matter

Dug Out Both Eyes and Rubbed in Lime

Lü Anchang Fled Afterwards

The Authorities Should Arrest and Punish Him Strictly

Lü Anchang from Yancheng, 35 years old, worked as a tea server at Yucai Public School on Shanhai Pass Road. His home was behind the reception hall at 20 Hemingfang on Xinjiang Road in Zhabei. Yesterday morning, the couple quarreled over a trivial matter. Lü Anchang then acted cruelly, gouging out Gao's eyes and rubbing lime into them. Gao fainted on the spot. Later, neighbors discovered it and immediately reported it to the patrol police. They took Gao to Renji Hospital for treatment. Chief Chen of the First Precinct of the Fourth District received the news and led the police to investigate. By then, the murderer had already fled without a trace. It is said that the couple had been married for many years and had a daughter named Yindi, seven years old. However, their relationship was extremely poor. Two years ago, Gao was abused and went to the Women's Association of this city for help. The association mediated, and Lü issued a written statement that he would not repeat the same actions. Regarding the gouging out of the eyes yesterday morning, it is said that there was more than one person involved. They first stuffed a towel into Gao's mouth to prevent her from shouting, and then carried out this cruel act. It is said that Gao was not at peace in the marriage, and her husband hated her to the extreme, so he took this drastic measure. The abandoned daughter, Yindi, has been transferred by the Public Security Bureau of the First Precinct of the Fourth District to the General Bureau for care. According to the doctor's examination, Gao's injuries are roughly as follows: Gao's eyes have both suffered severe injuries inside and out, with a lot of bleeding. The right eyeball has completely flowed out, leaving only an empty socket and already blind. The left eyeball suffered similar injuries, and it is difficult to predict whether it can be saved.

Vendetta on the Opium Couch

Luo Youlong Shot Three Times

A Stray Bullet Injured Zhao Er

Both Murderers Fled

At Chen Yunji Yanzike, downstairs in the east厢房 at 13 Baoxingli, Gongguan Road in the French Concession, at around 8:30 last night, a smoker named Luo Youlong went to smoke with two friends. Luo sat on opium couch number eight and called a waiter to bring two boxes of opium, smoking and talking. When the first box of opium was finished, the two friends took their leave. Shortly after the guests left, a man in a black satin长衫 suddenly came in and fired four shots at Luo with a pistol. After that he calmly left. Luo was shot three times, and the other bullet hit the leg of Zhao Er, a guest on opium couch number four. Afterwards, the owner of the opium den reported to the patrol police and took Luo and Zhao to Renji Hospital for treatment. It was found that two shots hit the chest and one hit the right hand, with very serious injuries. Zhao Er was shot in the left calf, which was a lighter wound. The French Concession patrol房 sent detectives to the scene to investigate and arrest the murderer. It is said that there were probably two murderers, one entered the room and one watched the door. The cause was probably a vendetta. After the injured Lu Youlong arrived at the hospital, he said that he lived at a friend's place on Zhoujiazui Road in Hongkou. No further information was given. Lu is 33 years old from Tianjin, and Zhao is 35 years old from Shandong.

Zhu Shisheng Died Tragically From Injuries

His Wife Has Been Convicted

Sentenced to Life Imprisonment

Zhang Xinglin Found Not Guilty

Zhu Shisheng, the local owner of Nanyang Department Store at No. 100 Yangzhou Road, argued with his wife, Zhang, over a trivial matter on the afternoon of the 24th of last month, became entangled on a rattan chair, and Zhu suddenly died from injuries. He was detained by the Yangshupu Patrol房 and sent to the First Special District Court. The interrogation was completed, and the verdict was awaited. This was reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefen presided over the Third Criminal Court and sentenced Zhu Zhang to life imprisonment. Another case in which Zhu Zhang hired a lawyer to sue her son-in-law Zhang Xinglin and Zhu Mengxing for injury was also heard yesterday morning by Judge Wu Tingqi in the Second Criminal Court. About 200 family members, relatives, and neighbors from both sides were present in court, and the court was full. The defendant Zhang Xinglin hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him in court. Zhu Mengxing did not appear. First, Judge Wu summoned the witnesses presented by Zhu Zhang, including Yang Changlin, A Tu, Chen Jiying, and Zhou Yuanchun. However, Yang and A Tu did not appear. Chen Jiying testified that he was 34 years old, from Changzhou, and was the accountant of Nanyang Department Store. The upstairs was the residence of Zhu Zhang and others, and the downstairs was the store. Judge Wu asked if he knew about the fight on July 24th. Chen replied that the shop owner Zhu Shisheng and his wife Zhu Zhang quarreled at around 5 pm. Because there was a funeral at that time, they were all drinking. He asked who was holding the funeral. He replied that it was the second daughter of the owner who died. He also heard the shop owner shouting for help. He asked if anyone hit Zhu Zhang at that time. He replied that yes. He asked who. He replied that he did not know. Witness Zhou Chunyuan also testified, saying that the defendant Zhang Xinglin happened to go to the funeral at that time and was not in the store. Zhu Haixin, the father of Zhu Mengxing, submitted a statement saying that his son had run away after quarreling with him before and had not returned since. Judge Wu then ordered the debate to begin. After the lawyer of Zhu Zhang and the defendant lawyer Fan Gang debated, Judge Wu ruled Zhang Xinglin not guilty and suspended the trial procedure for Zhu Mengxing. After the verdict, the sisters of Zhu Zhang all cried and left.

Opening of the Baxianqiao Branch

To facilitate the depositors of the two branches, the bank building was rushed to completion, and the cement pavement outside the door was not yet laid. Manager Xi is a well-known accountant who has been practicing in Shanghai for many years. He has experience in economics and banking and is especially amiable to customers. This branch has some special features compared to other branches, which are recorded as follows: (1) Safe deposit box: The bank is equipped with a safe deposit box with extremely strong construction. The door is made of pure steel and is about 5 inches thick. (Safety deposit boxes will be placed soon.) (2) Safe night deposit box: The bank is equipped with a safe night deposit box, which can be used by shops near Baxianqiao to deposit cash and banknotes after closing, and the surrounding area is a prosperous and lively area, so there is no danger when depositing. (3) Solicitation of picture answers: A very large colored picture is posted in the window of the bank, depicting two people, both holding savings books. One has a happy face, and the other has a sad face. The bank is soliciting answers from viewers, which will end on August 25th and be revealed in the window on September 1st. Savings gift certificates will be given as rewards. Overall, all the arrangements of the bank are aimed at facilitating customers, and the staff is also very energetic. The prosperity of the business in the future can be expected. After visiting, the reporter of this newspaper took several photos and attached them here. A brief history of Manager Xi is recorded as follows: Xi Yushu graduated from the Department of Special Business of Fudan University in Shanghai, with an honorary degree from the university. He was a backbone member of the Shanghai Student Union during the May Fourth Movement and was brave in taking responsibility. He served as a professor at Fudan University and Dongwu Law School, the chief of the General Affairs Section of the Anhui Provincial Coal and Oil Misunderstanding Department of the Ministry of Finance, and the chief accountant of the National Special Business Tax Office of the Fujian and Songjiang Salt Transport Envoy's Office. In recent years, he has been engaged in accounting business in Shanghai and has a good reputation.

Robbers Robbed Ice Factory in Pudong

At 0:40 yesterday (the 12th) morning, six robbers suddenly came to the Wujialong Welfare Ice Factory in Southeast Township of Hongzhen in Pudong (about four or five li from the town). Two of the robbers held pistols, and four robbers entered through the back door while two robbers were watching outside. After entering, they first fired two shots to show their power. One bullet hit the factory owner's right thumb. They pushed people into the inner room, recklessly searching and robbing, taking away more than 40 yuan in silver dollars, more than a dozen corners in small silver coins, dozens of copper coins, and several pieces of clothing. They left with the loot. It was not until 8:00 yesterday morning that the factory owner opened a list and reported it to the Hongzhen branch of the Third Precinct of the Fifth District for arrest. Patrol Officer Shi Lantian led the police to investigate for a week and returned. The police have been ordered to conduct a thorough search and arrest.

Intercepted a Runaway Apprentice

At around 3:30 yesterday morning, patrol officer Guo Shaoqu of post No. 15 of the First Precinct of the Sixth District on Robison Road in West Shanghai, who was on duty, suddenly saw a man about ten years old, carrying a bag of clothes and a rattan basket, running anxiously. Officer Guo, suspecting him of running in the middle of the night, stopped him for questioning. The man's face turned red and he hesitated. He was immediately detained and transferred to the Sixth District Police Station. After the district chief Ren's investigation, it was found that there were 110 yuan in banknotes, 10 yuan in silver dollars, 36 corners in small bills, 6 corners in small silver coins, and 12 pieces of coarse cloth clothing in the clothing bag. According to the man's confession, his name is Zhou Zilin, 16 years old, from Rugaogao, and he is an apprentice at the Liu Shunxing Tofu Shop in Sanjiaochang, Caojiadu. The silver dollars and clothes were stolen from the shop and taken with him to escape. After receiving the confession, District Chief Ren immediately sent the police to summon the shop owner Liu Heting to the station. After confirming the stolen goods were correct, he immediately issued a receipt to take them back. He then prepared a document and sent the apprentice to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Cotton Famine in Wusong

Due to the continuous rain during the early summer, all the cotton fields in the villages of Wusong were flooded, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. A famine has formed. The municipal committee office has received letters from Tu Di Bao Yu Fuhai and farmer Yang Jinchang of the district, stating that this year's early summer is when the cotton is developing, but the continuous rain has flooded everything, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. Seven or eight out of ten fields in each Tu area are low-lying, and only one or two are high-source areas. Only two or three out of ten families in each Tu area plant rice. In this situation, the residents of the Tu area rely on planting cotton to make a living, and their livelihoods have become hopeless. They earnestly request relief to help the people of Jiangsu, etc. After receiving the letters, the office sent personnel to the countryside to investigate, assess the severity, and prepare detailed registration forms. They were reported to the Land Bureau and the Social Bureau yesterday, requesting that personnel be sent again for reinvestigation to show the reality and facilitate relief.

Election Turmoil in the Women's Relief Association

Dispute Arises Over Recognition of District Representatives

According to the Riri News, the Women's Relief Association of this city was established on the 8th. Only five days later, a turmoil occurred yesterday due to the issue of election candidates. The details are as follows: Yesterday afternoon, Lin Kecong and Wang Xiaoying held a district representative meeting at Wu Ben Girls' School. Besides the two committee members, Huang Daping, Bao Guangyu, Zhang Xuefei, and others also arrived upon hearing the news. At that time, representatives from Districts 1, 2, 4, 6, and 7 had arrived. Lin Kecong then expressed his opinion, stating that District 7 was established after August 1st. According to the resolution, which stated that district associations must be established before August 1st, District 7, having been established after August 1st, naturally could not be recognized. At that time, Tang Naixin, Bao Guangyu, Huang Daping, Zhang Xuefei, and the other five committee members rose up in opposition, stating that if District 7 could not attend the election because it was established after August 1st, then District 6 was also established after August 1st, so why could it attend the election? The two sides began to debate. At that time, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters advocated that the elections for Districts 6 and 7 be suspended altogether. As a result, Huang Daping, Zhang Xuefei, Tang Naixin, Bao Guangyu, and the other four committee members withdrew from the meeting. More than ten attending representatives also withdrew one after another after seeing the four committee members withdraw, leaving very few. Lin Meiyan, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, declared that she would not be responsible for this type of election. Lin Kecong and others still issued ballots for the election. As a result, the election was hastily completed. The list of elected directors could not be ascertained.

Various Charitable Organizations

Telegrams Received from Various Provinces Requesting Aid for Flood Victims

Red Cross Society: The Chinese Red Cross Society received telegrams requesting aid yesterday, which are summarized as follows: (1) Respected heads of the Shanghai Red Cross Society: Heaven is unkind and sends this great calamity. Our town is located outside the West Gate of Anqing. During this continuous rainfall, the farmers and tenants tried their best to protect it, and fortunately it was preserved. Unexpectedly, in recent days, there has been heavy rain for three days and nights. The mountain torrents in the Wan River have erupted, and the river tide has risen sharply by three feet, exceeding the water level of the 27th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty. The northwest embankment of our town has collapsed for more than a hundred zhang. Thousands of farmers and tenants gathered to protect it desperately, but the rain was too heavy, and the water level was deep both inside and outside, with no place to get soil. Therefore, it collapsed on the night of the 24th of last month. The water surged and rushed directly into the southern embankment. Countless houses in the town were washed away, and food, livestock, and equipment were washed away. Thousands of men, women, old and young in the whole town were unable to escape and were drowned, with dozens of deaths. At present, the disaster-stricken farmers are gathered on the embankment, without clothes or food, exposed to the wind and eating in the open air. The situation is urgent. It is found that Guangji Town has also collapsed. Before the collapse, the provincial and county governments supervised the rescue efforts. After the collapse, the government also properly handled the relief and accommodation. More than 10,000 refugees in our town, with 44,000 mu of farmland, have no house, no home, no clothes, and no food, and are extremely distressed. In addition to requesting the Anhui Provincial Government and Huaining County Government to allocate funds for relief, we respectfully recommend representative Xu Pingxuan to request your association to send personnel for inspection and to allocate relief funds as appropriate for emergency relief, so that the lives of more than 10,000 people can be saved from the ravines. We anxiously await your order. Farmers Cao Qingquan, Chen Jinghua, Wu Chunshan, Zhang Baozhen, etc. of the Guangcheng Town, Haikou Zhou, Huaining County, Anhui, and more than 10,000 others kowtow and weep. (2) Respected President of the Shanghai Chinese Red Cross Society: On the evening of the day before last month, the Liu River flooded, and the city has become a swamp. Houses and fields along the river have been damaged, and many people and animals have been washed away. The cries for help have been incessant for days. Our branch has sent lifeboats to patrol the river and provide rescue, and has also donated porridge to help the refugees, but our ability is weak and the disaster is serious. We deeply feel the insignificance of a cup of water to a cart of firewood. The General Assembly has great love in its heart. We sincerely request that you find ways to provide relief to benefit the disaster-stricken people. We hereby send a telegram to inform you. We implore you to consider it. Gao Chengzong, President of the Liuzhou Red Cross Branch, and Zhou Shu, Vice President, kowtow.

After the war and famine years, it was followed by hail, and after the hail, there is now flooding due to continuous rain. Since the beginning of summer, it has been raining continuously for days. The mountain torrents in the upper reaches have erupted, and the rivers and ditches are full due to the surging water, so that even places far from the river and along the river have become swamps. Corpses are floating in the water, and starving people commit suicide, which is often heard. The drowning of livestock, the collapse of houses, and the submergence of fields cannot be counted. The disaster-stricken people who have come to the city to seek refuge are supporting the old and carrying the young, and their cries shake the sky. Recently, there has been heavy rain that has not stopped for several days, and more than ten zhang of the city wall have collapsed again, and everyone is in danger. A survey shows that 95% of the county has been flooded, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. Fields, houses, people, and livestock have been washed away, and a vast expanse of water has become a swamp. Those who have not died from drowning will die from starvation. Since July of this year, there has been continuous rain for a whole month, causing many sections of the city wall to collapse and countless houses to collapse. The water level is several feet deep on the plains, and ruined walls are everywhere. We still hope that

the autumn harvest will be fruitful, so that we can make up for the losses a little. Unexpectedly, the lake water has risen again, and the damage is even greater. The harvest of early and late rice is hopeless, and the amount of loss is incalculable. At present, the farmers in various places not only have no surplus in their granaries, but also have no food to eat. Moreover, their villages have become swamps, and they have nowhere to live. The tragic situation is difficult to describe in full.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce

Minutes of the National Goods Market Committee

The National Goods Market of the Commodity Exhibition Hall of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce convened the fifth meeting of the National Goods Market Committee at 3:00 p.m. on August 6th. Those present included Zheng Chengqing, Ye Xiaoshan, Ding Xunhao, Fang Jiange, Xi Guansheng, and ten others. Zhu Dechao was the chairman, and Zhong Jinchen was the recorder. The agenda is recorded below: (1) During the period of boycotting Japanese goods, this market intends to expand publicity. How should the expenses be raised? Decision: Approve the expansion of publicity, but recently the weather has been hot. If it is held urgently, there may be no significant effect. It must be decided in September. The method of raising funds will be discussed separately. (2) Should the service of the market's sales staff be subject to regulations established by this market to ensure compliance? Decision: Sales staff should be subject to regulations while working in this market. The regulations will be named "Sales Staff Service Guidelines of This Market." (3) Determine the opening date of the second-floor market and the sections that should be added. Decision: The opening date is set for the Double Tenth Festival this year. If preparations are not completed by then, the opening may be postponed to November 1st. The sections that should be added are as follows: copper and iron beds, music, clocks and glasses, small hardware, porcelain, cloisonné, stationery, tobacco and alcohol, candy and small sundry goods, woodenware, shoes and hats. (4) Temporary proposals: Mr. Pei Weimin proposed the printing of wrapping paper. Decision: The wrapping paper must be printed with the names of various factories and stores in a mixed manner. The market office will print it on behalf of the factories and stores. The expenses will be shared according to the stalls, but it must be implemented when the second-floor market opens. Mr. Zhu Tingchao proposed hiring experts to give lectures. Decision: In order to increase the knowledge of the sales staff, this market may hire experts with rich business experience to give lectures at appropriate times. The location and date will be announced at that time.

In accordance with Article 2 of the Central Bank's convertible note regulations, the cash reserve should be 60% and the guarantee reserve should be 40%. New Kang Disaster Victims' Families

Emergency Meeting Held Yesterday

The New Kang Steamer Disaster Victims' Families Association convened a meeting of all family members in Shanghai yesterday afternoon. More than 200 men, women, old and young attended the meeting. Mr. Zhu, a member of the Standing Committee, was elected as chairman to report on the case. More than two years have passed since the incident occurred on July 21, 1929. During these two years, we have repeatedly sent letters and telegrams to the Central Government, the National Government, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Communications, and various national organizations, appealing and begging for help. We have also petitioned in Beijing three times. Although the government authorities and the people of the whole country have expressed deep sympathy and given us their utmost concern, the international environment has ultimately not been adequately resolved, causing the dead to die unjustly at the bottom of the sea and the living to cry in pain in the world. Thinking of this, we are heartbroken and weeping. Subsequently, according to international practice, in the event of a maritime disaster, a lawsuit for damages may be filed in the local court in accordance with the law. Therefore, following the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, we filed a lawsuit for damages with the First Local Court of the Shanghai Special District. The enthusiasm and righteousness of the two great lawyers, Wu Jingxiong and Sheng Zhenwei, are not only admired by the members of this association, but also welcomed by the people of the whole country who are concerned about this case. The case has now been scheduled for trial in the Ninth Division of the Special Court at 8:00 a.m. on the 15th of this month. We ask everyone to discuss at length how everything should proceed in the future. Family members spoke one after another, and their anger overflowed in their words. The old, the young, and the women were especially moved to tears. After discussion, it was decided: (1) All family members of the disaster victims in Shanghai should attend the trial in court. (2) Request the court to expedite the trial of this case within the possible scope. (3) Regarding the issue of litigation assistance, the court should consider the circumstances and approve the assistance. (4) Petition the National Government and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to abolish all unequal treaties between China and Japan and cancel the navigation rights of Japanese ships. (5) Send telegrams to various national organizations to continue to strive for assistance. (6) Telegraph and call on the people at home and abroad not to take Japanese ships or load Japanese ships. (7) Warn the Japanese shipping companies not to spread false information. (8) Send letters to the two lawyers, Wu Jingxiong and Sheng Zhenwei. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

The Main Criminal in the Case of Forging for Pawn

Zhou Yugong Released on Bail for Re-examination

Zhou Yugong, a Chaozhou native living in the Boxiang Village on Lafayette Road in the French Concession, colluded with his cohabiting relatives, Ding Xu and Ding Ding, to pawn counterfeit gold bracelets and rings at the Yitai Pawnshop on Lafayette Road three times, receiving 115 yuan in foreign currency. After the case was discovered, Yitai was arrested. Detective Zeng Juru arrested Ding Xu and Ding Ding. However, Zhou, upon hearing the news, fled to Tongzhou. Xu and his relatives were taken to the former Joint Court for interrogation, where they confessed that they were entrusted by Zhou to pawn the items. The official, considering that Xu and the women were fooled, sentenced them to probation and released them. He also ordered the seizure of Zhou's property and ordered Zhou to report to the case within one month for investigation. Zhou hired a lawyer and reported to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Criminal Division of the Second Special Court for questioning. First, the lawyer of the police station, Fei Xizhen, explained the case. Then, Zeng Juru, the detective in charge of the case, explained the previous situation and claimed that he had found out that the defendant Zhou had pawned counterfeit items at the Hongtai Pawnshop on Lagenna Road. After the case was discovered, Chen Ziliang, who exchanged the money, mediated with Hongtai and repaid the pawn principal, with a written statement. He is now summoning witnesses to the case for questioning. However, Ding Xu and others have moved elsewhere and cannot be summoned. According to the witness Zhu, a clerk at the Yitai Pawnshop, an old woman came to pawn the items three times. The defendant was also in the shop when she came for the first time, and he estimated the price and pawned it for 70 yuan. He came to pawn the items twice later and mixed through each time. After he found out, he reported the arrest and arrested the old woman, who confessed that Zhou had asked them to pawn the items. I know the defendant. According to Wang Xiaocheng, a clerk at the Hongtai Pawnshop, the defendant pawned ornaments for a total of 570 yuan. After the discovery, his brother asked Chen Ziliang to mediate and repay the pawn principal of 350 yuan. Chen Ziliang also proved the mediation process. Zhou Gongyu confessed that he was in the second-hand goods business and bought a piece of gold jewelry for 7 yuan and sold it to his cohabiting relative, Ding Xu, for 9 yuan. He denied entrusting them to pawn the counterfeit items and hired a lawyer to defend him. Judge Ma Shounan verified the confession and ordered the defendant to pay 200 yuan in cash bail for a re-examination on August 19.

Page 17

Free Talk

World Tidbits

— Sea Rover

The Inventors of Four Things

One day in London, a gentleman wearing glasses, a soft felt hat, and a cork leg hobbled onto a public carriage. A good educator took this as good material to test the common sense of his students. He asked who invented the glasses, cork leg, public carriage, and soft felt hat.

The inventor of the glasses was an Italian named S.D. Armati, born in the thirteenth century. There is a house on a street in Florence, marked with a stone by the Technicians' Association to commemorate him.

Originally, artificial legs were not made of cork. Later, Dr. Cork invented the use of cork for manufacturing them, which made them much lighter for the disabled. However, the English word for cork is "Cork," and the inventor's name just happened to be Cork. This is too much of a coincidence. Perhaps his name was misspelled.

The public carriage was a French invention. In 1667, the great philosopher Pascal had the privilege of operating public carriages in Paris. However, although they were public, there were restrictions. Only members of the upper class were allowed to ride. Soldiers and servants were generally rejected.

Felt was invented by the Tartar people thousands of years ago. Almost all of the houses, clothing, bedding, etc. in North Asia are made of felt.

Record of an Unusual Meteorite

— Changsheng

In the sixth year of the Republic, I served in the army in Jialing and was ordered to temporarily serve as the magistrate of Langzhong for only seventeen days. With ample time after official duties, I wandered around the mountains and rivers. The place was the Zhengnan Gate, which had been closed for many years. People came and went through the East and West Gates. Outside the East Gate was the Great Silk Market. In previous years, magnificent houses lined the streets, but due to years of war, there were only rubble and hills. Simple sheds were built on the original sites to meet the needs of the market. The silks on display were all coarse and inferior. As it was approaching summer, I selected several pieces of silk to make summer clothes. Going out of the West Gate, less than a hundred steps away, was the Wanyuan Dam. The construction of this dam was very peculiar. It sloped down like a shark fin or stone steps. Steps were carved into a ladder. It was about thirty li long. There were countless stone rhinoceroses in the water, chanting in the wind and howling at the moon, swallowing and spitting out waves. It was truly a useful tool for preventing floods and a powerful enemy for fighting dragons. This place was the Jialing River. In the past, when Emperor Ming of Tang fled the rebellion of An Lushan, he traveled far to western Sichuan. He had passed by the Jialing River and admired it endlessly. Later, he ordered Wu Daozi to paint it on a screen. At that time, his entourage, such as Du Fu, were all exiles in Lizhou and wrote many poems. The current Shi Kuige Pavilion is located downstream of the Wanyuan Dam. There is a copper rhinoceros outside the pavilion. The pavilion houses the Lord of Sichuan, a beardless youth with a face like a beautiful woman. Two inscriptions are written with Du Fu's Shi Kuige poem. The handwriting is the same as He Zijhen's biography of the black woman, but it is unsigned. I dare not be sure. Behind the courtyard is a meteorite stone, about two feet high. Touching it, it is slightly warm. The words "Meteorite" are engraved on it. The history of the meteorite is written on the wall. In February of the fourteenth year of Chongzhen of the Ming Dynasty, a star fell on the Shi Kuige Pavilion. The remaining fire shot in all directions, and the buildings were reduced to ashes. For more than a month, no one dared to pass by. In the eighth year of Yongzheng, a great flood occurred. With the remaining labor from repairing the dam, the Shi Kuige Pavilion was rebuilt, and the meteorite was placed in the temple as a permanent memorial. There are many meteorites in various provinces. They are only seen in books and history. None of the stones remain. Only the Tongjing in Beijing has a fallen star stone. According to an old man nearby, "it glows at night." However, the Tongjing's fallen star stone crumbles when cut. As for the Shi Kuige Pavilion's meteorite, it is harder than iron and its texture is different from stone. Although the words "Meteorite" are engraved on it, it only has a rough form. This is a meteorite that I have personally seen. The stone is still in the Shi Kuige Pavilion in Langzhong. Those who pass by can go there in person. Not only are the mountains and rivers beautiful and the historical sites famous, but the meteorite is also worth lingering over for days. Across the river is Jinping Mountain, where Zhang Daoling and his wife attained enlightenment and ascended to heaven on the same day. A few hundred steps further is the South Gate. There is a couplet on the gate: "Three hundred li of Jialing River, Twelve Buildings in the Garden." This is a factual record.

A Strange Wedding

— Mo Yi

British famous photography journalist Mr. Hu Bu published an essay "A strange wedding" on the April London newspaper. The content described the wedding Hu Bu witnessed when he was travelling in Buza (a kind of half-civilized Hui minority group). It is rather interesting, and translated as follows.

I (the author's pronoun, similar below) only just entered their village and I felt an odd mood. Let alone their houses, they were the same as in primordial times. They were constructed of very thick bamboo held together, high off the ground. The building materials were all grass and mud. From far away they resembled a bird's nest. Everyone's clothing, whether man or woman, all wore a kind of shining, and also red, green, and other colors, robe that went all the way to the ground. The style of the clothes was not like the Chinese's clothing, nor like a monk's clothing. There were seven stitches and eight patches, and I did not know how they made it.

It just so happened that the second day I was there, I encountered them holding a wedding. Therefore, I got to witness a bizarre wedding. Normally outsiders are not allowed to participate. Later, I do not know how many procedures were undergone, many flattering things were said, and many valuable gifts were given, before they allowed me. Their relatives and friends had to stay at the groom's house for at least two days. During these two days, they ate, drank, and danced to their heart's content, as if it were an earned right.

They viewed marriage as an extremely important event in their lives. Therefore, they took it very seriously. But most of them were poor. The groom had to save money and use it sparingly for several months before marriage. If it was temporarily not enough, he had to borrow money to pay for the wedding expenses. The bride did not need to borrow money, but she had to provide the groom with the money she had saved up on ordinary days to prepare for any eventuality.

What surprised me the most was that the bride's father carried the bride on his shoulders and walked down the bamboo ladder step by step, while the groom supported her right hand. The groom was only seventeen years old, and the bride was twenty years old. Looking at their appearance, they seemed like a pair of siblings. (Because their houses are high off the ground, they had to use ladders to go up and down). She didn't look like an ordinary woman at all. Her hair was styled with an unknown headdress in a never-before-seen way. Her lips were painted as red as blood. Her eyelids were painted blue. According to their customs, the bride's feet must not touch the ground. Within three days of the wedding, she always sat on the shoulders of her father or uncle. She also had to keep her eyes tightly closed. Only on the fourth day could she open them. Otherwise, unexpected misfortune would befall the newlyweds.

Then, her father sat her on a high chair. The groom stood on the left. Relatives and friends surrounded them, shouting and dancing, like a large group of injured beasts howling and jumping in anger. Thus, the wedding was completed. A pair of strangers became husband and wife.

A Description of Shanghai

— Miao Yu

When I first came to Shanghai, I couldn't help but be filled with eager admiration. Now that I've lived here for a long time, I've begun to realize that Shanghai is worthy of cursing. I recall a friend, Su Feng, who wrote a new-style poem satirizing it. The words went: "The first day, I saw the busy crowds. The second day, I saw the leaping gold. The third day, I saw demons and monsters. After that, I never saw any light." Although not a detailed description, it is extremely insightful.

Shanghai society is almost a large entertainment arena. The masses in society are all actors in makeup taking the stage. There are so many plays performed. The social news in the newspapers, page after page, are all scripts. However, this is only a kind of comical imagination. In fact, it is rare to see a penetrating depiction of Shanghai society on the stage or screen. Why is this?

First, old playwrights like to make superficial observations. For example, when describing a dancer, they only know that she is a dancer, without asking how she became a dancer. Or, when describing the life of a dancer, they only know that she revolves around music and lights, without asking about her inner heart and the bitterness of tears. Thus, they beat around the bush, and the taste is like chewing wax.

Second, old playwrights only care about the excitement and disregard the intricacies of the plot. For example, when describing a dance hall, the hair ornaments and clothing, the overlapping shoes, this is certainly lively. However, dancing with each other without any twists and turns, what meaning is there?

Therefore, a good playwright does not focus on one aspect in their description, and the plot does not adhere to one side. They make the script as blazing as fire, the plot as cloudy as mist. They make the actors like dragons soaring into the sky. Thus, it is lively and tortuous, and the actors can fully express their genius, and the script is thus successful.

Today's Chinese cinema has also been immersed in the tide of sound films. We see the shortcomings of Western sound films, which lie in only desiring excitement and neglecting the plot. Therefore, the way to success for domestic sound films is to vigorously correct this flaw. Recently, the Star Film Company produced a large sound film, "Such is Paradise." It is purely based on Shanghai society as the background and makes a subtle satire. Now that this film is about to be released, I hope that it will not be bombarded by viewers with the words "sensual" and "glamorous." What can make people unwilling to miss this good film is that this film's power can naturally evoke wild laughter and natural tears, and once again allow people to obtain endless satisfaction and return home, forever engraved in their minds, and say with a refreshing feeling, "Such is paradise, such is paradise."

Indian Travelogue (79)

— Ling Hua

The great Muslim writer Mirza Abullazl gifted me his work, "The Biography of Muhammad and a Record of Muhammad's Words and Deeds." I use it to understand the life of Muslims. I wish Chinese people would know that it is difficult for Muslims and Indians to get along, but Muslims and Chinese people can easily assimilate. I have studied the books on the nature of the universe in the Muslim religion and know that its origins are similar to those of Daoism in their tranquility. Its systems of governance and military laws are similar to Confucianism. Respect for heaven and ancestors, strength and self-reliance, are similar to the Yellow Emperor's founding of the country and the wise rulers of the Han and Tang dynasties. Its rule over Europe, the Middle East, and Central Asia for one or two thousand years continues to flourish and cannot be easily disregarded. Whether Russification can be carried out in Europe will depend on Germany. Whether it can be carried out in Asia will depend on the Muslims. As for the situation of the Indian people, they are the most enthusiastic about being close to China. Even towards the Japanese, there is some insincerity because they are narrow-minded and think of seizing things. The Chinese are just a middle ground. They can unite the Buddhist, Indian, and Muslim races, then Asia will be easy to unite. If America is added, then Asia will be united. The Europeans will join last and the situation of the world's grand union will be set. The novice monk Shenxin told me that the principles of world aesthetics like complexity and dislike simplicity. If people combine various sects and priests of various religions to organize, then they can also be beautiful. For thousands of years, China has only talked about the three religions. I am concerned about its narrowness. Now it is appropriate to add the Muslim, Christian, and Hindu religions to make five religions. Also, adopt the strengths of Marx, etc., to apply them to our people's livelihood doctrine to achieve the great union. This is the responsibility of us Chinese people. If we want to achieve great unity, we must start from intermarriage between different races, religions, and classes. Then everything will be resolved and assimilated.

The study of the Muslim invasion of India has two causes: one is going from the northwest and southeast to plunder its resources; the other is to spread Islam. Therefore, wherever they went, the Indian and Buddhist religions were destroyed without remainder. To this day, the Indians are not happy with its rise. From Arabia, Arabia is the meaning of language, the meaning of wasteland and desert. When Islam rose, Arabia was polytheistic, with women being kidnapped into prostitution. If there were people who practiced monogamy, they would be ashamed because they were poor and lowly. Women's status was very low. The custom of killing daughters was prevalent. They worshiped gods of the sun, moon, stones, and trees. There were three levels of moon goddesses: one was the black moon, one was the white moon, and one was the middle-level moon. When people died, a female camel was tied to their tomb, not given food or drink, and left to die because it would serve them. There was also Christianity, but at that time it was corrupt and mixed with polytheism, which could not be avoided. Based on this kind of scene, and with each department under foreign rule, the monotheism of the Muslims rose in response. It is said that when Islam rose, the world was extremely unrestrained and degenerate. I see that Muslims pray several times a day, and the long prayers involve more than a hundred prostrations. This is training for the spirit of the army, and hard work and creation are not easy. Japanese people comment on Lenin as being the Muhammad of the 20th century, meaning that he was hardworking. The asceticism of Hinduism tends towards gentleness, while the endurance of Islam is attributed to strength. The bitterness of human life is the same.

Speaking of the Rotary Club

Women, Women (18)

— Yao Su Feng

Xiao Rong couldn't hold back anymore. He had already forgotten that he was his parents' son, his wife's husband, and only knew that he was Miss Ding's lover. He actually raised his voice to his father and said, "Don't make a fuss with me! Don't even give me face! To be honest, that woman has a lot of money! If I keep staying in this house, do you want me to pull a rickshaw? You can't control me! Huh!"

"Shameless! How could you say such a thing! We sent you to Shanghai to study, not to be a gigolo! What does it matter if she has money! Besides, you can't be so brazen! Think about it! When you came back the day before yesterday, what did you take out with you? Your face doesn't deserve such nonsense!" Xiao Rong's father finally burst into abuse. Xiao Rong's mother really couldn't stand it either. She said, "Xiao Rong! I always thought you were a serious scholar! Who knew you would say such absurd things! You never come home with a good face, but you come back to make your parents suffer! Think about it, you've been in Shanghai for a year. How much money have you spent? Where did all that money come from? Now don't talk so fiercely! Just return the pieces of gold jewelry you took the day before yesterday, and I'll let you go enjoy yourself! It's like, having a son like you is worse than not having one at all!" She was so angry that her voice trembled.

Xiao Rong was somewhat embarrassed and angry. Although he knew he was wrong, he didn't want to admit a single mistake. He just said, "Fine! Why bother like this? If I don't come back, you send the shop assistant to look for me. When I come back, you bang the table and slap the bench and give me a lecture! Fine! I don't want to listen!" As he spoke, he flew out the door.

"Wait! You can't leave!"

"Don't let Xiao Rong leave!"

Xiao Rong's father and mother both chased after him, but he was nowhere to be seen. They turned back angrily, one sighing, one crying bitterly.

Not long after, Xiao Rong's wife also returned with her flower basket. Auntie Matchmaker told her everything that had just happened, and she cried in anger too.

Later, after everyone discussed it, they felt that they had to find Xiao Rong and bring him back. Xiao Rong's wife volunteered and immediately rushed to the Railway Hotel. Fortunately, she usually went there to sell flowers every day, so everyone inside was very familiar with her. When she arrived at the Railway Hotel, she first asked the cashier, "Are there two guests here—a man and a woman—who came from Shanghai yesterday? The man is wearing a yellow suit, and the woman has permed hair and is wearing a red cheongsam. What room are they in?"

The cashier saw that it was the woman who often came to sell flowers, thought for a moment, and said, "Yes, there are. They're probably in room thirty-two. It's just that they've already returned to Shanghai today!"

Gold Price Drops Eight Taels

Fluctuations Reached Over Ten Taels: Yesterday, the twelve markers of gold prices resumed their downward trend, and the state was chaotic and greatly volatile. From morning to noon, there were fluctuations of more than ten taels. In the afternoon, there was only a fluctuation of two or three taels. In the end, it fell by eight taels, a reverse of the two-day rise. There were mostly sellers in the market. The price opened low because silver bars suddenly rose. Afterwards, due to active buying, there was an effort to raise it from all directions. Since foreign exchange rates strengthened, they turned from weak to sharp, and again jumped over the 780 tael mark. Suddenly, it was heard that Mr. Pittman was returning to the United States from China and planned to request President Hoover to issue a plan to rescue silver prices. The market was panicked by this news. Each firm tended to sell off and a storm arose, going from bad to worse, and plummeting more than ten taels. Later, because it was Wednesday, there was no market for foreign exchange, so there were no special changes.

Formerly Hit by News: From the morning, the September opening fell 5.4 taels, at 776.2 taels. Large bars rose slightly by one-sixteenth. The forecast on the previous evening was that prices would not fall. Also, US stocks rose, but silver prices did not move. Thus, sellers were very vigorous. Tong Taichang, Senchang, Yongri, Changshun, Shunli, Wanxing, Bingxing, etc., all sold off. The price then fell to 73 taels, after which Yuanxing, Yongzhi, Fengyong, Wupin, Chengfeng, Yonyong, Yongheng, etc., all entered. The price was then raised by two or three taels. The initial quoted price was 75.78 taels, and the posted price was the same as before, then increased to 78.45 taels. Domestic English gold was stable, closing at 5625, and Zhengjin absorbed November at 5625. Not long after, Yongfeng, Tong Taichang, Daxing, Yonglai sold off. When the price retreated to 75.5 taels, Yongheng, Richang, Yifeng, Yongda, Decheng, Xinheng, Hengyu, Yuanmao, Yong, etc., competed to buy, and English gold recovered, closing at only 4375, so in just half an hour it rose sharply by more than 7 taels. In between, there was a slight fluctuation of one or two taels, reaching 83 taels by 10:20 AM. Unfortunately, it was a flash in the pan and was about to decline. The bank was still willing to sell English gold at a halfpenny, and Fuyu, Hengyu, Yongfeng, Qianchang, Xiang, Yuanheng, Bingxing, Richang, Changsheng, Yong, etc., constantly sold off. Especially because the United States was about to open a bill to relieve the silver shortage, the industry suddenly showed a state of terror. The price then plunged more than ten taels in a waterfall-style fall until noon, finally reaching 70.03 taels. By the close, it was 72.2 taels, and it continued to do business at 2.5 to 3 taels. The posted price was 819 taels, and the small difference was from 43 to 44 taels to 36 to 37 taels. The noon close was 47 taels.

No Major Changes in the Later Market: The afternoon market opened at 71.5 taels, followed by 1.2 taels. Afterwards, the Indian exchange rate rose in the near term and fell in the long term, reaching 73.5 taels. Then it was suppressed by seven or eight cents, and Fuxing, Yong, and Richang came to enter. At 2:15 PM, it was 74.8 taels. After that, there were slight advances and retreats, and the market was stable. Because there was no market for exchange drafts on Wednesday, there were also few transactions on the desk. Until after 3:00 PM, there seemed to be more sellers, retreating to 2.78 taels. In an instant, the wind and clouds rose, and the Indian exchange rate reported a small five anna. Qianchang, Xiang, Yuanmao, Yong, Yifeng, Yong, etc., took the stage and dropped their hands and entered. In just over ten minutes, the price increased by more than three taels, and at 3:30 PM, it was 76.2 taels. However, Tong Taichang, Shunli, etc., still sold off, so it was difficult to stand firm, and it fell again by more than three taels. At 4:15 PM, it was 72.8 taels. By the 4:30 PM close, it was 73.7 taels. Importantly, there was again a transaction of more than 4 taels, which was a head-covering entry, a pullback of 7.9 taels compared to the previous day (according to the listed price).

Spot Market Shape is Relatively Good: According to the maximum price of 83 taels for the whole day, and the minimum price of 70.03 taels, there was a difference of 12.7 taels. Goods were at 5.8 taels in the early morning market, 2 taels at the noon close, 1.8 taels in the afternoon, and 4.5 taels at the close. The posted price was from 47 to 44 or 45 taels, and registered at 70 to 72 taels. The water supplement was 7 taels, 72 taels in the afternoon. Spot red bars added 11 taels to 10.05 taels, better than the previous day. Yingfeng Heng bought more than 1,000 taels, which were sold by the same industry, and the firm resold 1,000 taels to the Tianjin gang.

Mostly Speculators Exiting: As for the transactions of each firm on the desk, Yuanmao Yong, Zhifeng Yong, Wanxing, Yongheng, Xinheng, Futaiheng, Fuxing Yong, Chengfeng Yong, and Yuanxing Yong all entered. Senchang Yong, Richang, Tong Taichang, Shunli, Yongfeng, Bingxing, Daxing Yong, Qianchang Xiang, Yuanheng, Cuichang Yong, and Fuyu all exited. Cotton Yarn: Yarn Market Situation Slightly Stabilized

The yarn market trend is slightly stabilized because after a big drop, profit-takers are covering their short positions. In the 暗 (àn, dark/unofficial) market, there is a slight increase in demand for coarse yarn from Yunnan merchants, and the selling price is 3-4 taels higher than the standard yarn. Therefore, there is some intention to recoup losses, which is good. However, considering the world situation, there is no hope of a large increase. It would not be surprising if there were a slight pullback. The trend may temporarily fluctuate, but overseas cotton prices are very low, and there is still a large profit to be made from 10-count coarse yarn for textile mills. Therefore, some manufacturers are hedging forward positions. The future situation remains ordinary.
